The Sign of Determination in Prayer Intent
A practical test for the presence of definite intention in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the sign of determination ('alāmat al-ta‘yīn) to assess the presence of intention in prayer for fatwa purposes.

Core Idea
A definite intention is present if one can answer what prayer they are performing without hesitation.

Intention (niyyah) is a condition for the validity of prayer, but how can a mufti verify its presence? The Hanafi school provides a practical test: the person must be able to instantly state which prayer they are starting. This lesson explains this rule and its application in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the moment of assessment
The test is applied before the takbīr taḥrīmah, when the intention is being formed.
Do not ask during the prayer itself.
2
Ask the question
Politely ask the person: 'Which prayer are you about to begin?'
The tone should be neutral to avoid distress.
3
Observe the response
Note whether the person answers immediately without hesitation or pauses to think.
Hesitation includes any delay, stammering, or asking for clarification.
4
Apply the rule
If the answer comes instantly, the intention is present. If hesitation occurs, the intention is considered absent and the prayer may be invalid.
This is the 'alāmat al-ta‘yīn.
5
Issue the fatwa
Advise the person to make a firm intention and repeat the prayer if already performed without proper intention.
If the person is a repeat offender, counsel them on the importance of niyyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قالوا وعلامة الشعبين بالصلوة ان تكونَ بِخَيْك لَوْ سُئِلَ إِلى صَلَاةٍ تُصَلَّى يُمْكِنه ان يحب بلا تامل ترجمه اختبار فرماتے ہیں نماز کی تعیین کی علامت یہ ہے کہ اگر معلوم کیا جائے کہ کون سی نماز پڑھا رہے ہوتو و وہ بغیر سوچے جواب دیدے۔ تشریح: استحضار نیت اور تعیین کی علامت یہ ہے کہ اگر نماز شروع کرنے سے پیشتر نماز پڑھنے والے سے دریافت کیا جائے تم کون کی نماز پڑھا رہے ہو تو وہ بلا تامل اور غور و فکر کے بغیر جواب دیدے اور اگر وہ تو قف کرے؟ اور سوچنے کی ضرورت پڑے گی تو سمجھا جائے گا کہ اس کی نیت حاضر نہیں ہے۔
They said: The sign of determination in prayer is that if he is asked 'which prayer are you praying?' he can answer without hesitation. Translation: The scholars state that the sign of determination in prayer is that if asked what prayer he is performing, he answers without thinking. Commentary: The sign of presence of intention and determination is that if before starting the prayer, the person is asked 'which prayer are you praying?' he answers without hesitation or thought; if he hesitates and needs to think, it is understood that his intention is not present.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage provides a practical rasm (definitional rule) for the presence of definite intention (ta‘yīn) in prayer. It states that if a person is asked what prayer they are about to perform, they should be able to answer immediately without reflection. This indicates that their intention is present and specific. If they hesitate or need to think, it shows their intention is not properly present. This rule is useful for self-assessment and for a mufti to judge the validity of one's prayer: if a person cannot state their intention quickly, their prayer may be invalid due to lack of proper niyyah.

Key Terms
علامة التعيين (‘alāmat al-ta‘yīn): The sign that one's intention is specific and present: ability to answer without hesitation.
استحضار النية (istiḥḍār al-niyyah): Having the intention present in the mind at the start of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person begins prayer but when asked, 'What prayer are you praying?' they pause to think. What does this indicate according to the Hanafi rule?
A) The prayer is still valid because intention is in the heart.
B) The intention is not properly present, potentially invalidating the prayer.
C) The prayer becomes supererogatory.
D) The person must repeat the prayer without hesitation.

Key Takeaway
A practical test for definite intention: the ability to answer without hesitation indicates presence; hesitation indicates absence.

Friday Prayer with Zuhr Intention
Ruling on Friday prayer with Zuhr intention.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to APPLY the Hanafi ruling that Friday prayer is valid with Zuhr intention to a fatwa scenario, and EVALUATE the disagreement between the two shaykhs and Imam Zufar.

Core Idea
Friday prayer is valid even if intended as Zuhr — the substitute inherits the ruling of the original.

This lesson examines a classic Hanafi dispute on intention in Friday prayer. The two shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) held that if one prays Friday with the intention of Zuhr, the prayer is valid, because Zuhr is the original obligation and Friday is its substitute. Imam Zufar disagreed, arguing that the substitute cannot be performed with the intention of the original. Understanding this debate clarifies the Hanafi principle of substitution (ibdal) and its practical implications for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the disputed ruling
What is the act? Friday prayer. What is the dispute? Whether it is valid if one intends it as Zuhr. Note the two different positions.
The act is the same; the difference is in the intention.
2
Parse the two shaykhs' position
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, Friday is a substitute for Zuhr on Friday. Intending the original (Zuhr) suffices for the substitute. Therefore the prayer is valid.
They consider Zuhr the original obligation.
3
Parse Imam Zufar's opposing view
Imam Zufar holds that Friday is the substitute, and one cannot intend the original to perform the substitute. So intending Zuhr invalidates Friday.
He sees Friday as the substitute and Zuhr as replaced.
4
Parse the later tarjih (mufta bihi)
The later preferred view (as cited from Kanz al-Daqaiq) agrees with the two shaykhs: Friday is valid with Zuhr intention, but it is better to intend Friday specifically.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
5
Apply the principle to a fatwa scenario
Suppose a person realizes during prayer that they intended Zuhr instead of Friday. According to the mufta bihi, the prayer is valid. Advise them accordingly.
The principle of substitution (ibdal) justifies the validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ور ٹرک میں بہتہ جمعہ فرض ہے جس کو شروع کر دے وہی فرض ہے۔ علامہ حموی کا رجحان اس طرف ہے کہ جمعہ میں ہے اور خبر دی ہے۔ الا بھی المحمومة سے پہلے مصنف نے فرمایا تھا فرض الوقت اور وقت الظہر ایک ہی حکم میں ہے لیکن اگر کسی نے جوری که زمین فرغل وقت کمدی تو شیخین کے نزدیک جمعہ کے دن فرض الوقت کی نیت درست ہو جائے گی کیونکہ ان کے ازاد یک جمعہ کے دن جمعے کی نماز ہی اصل ہے اور ظہر جمعہ فوت ہونے کے بعد بدل بن سکتی ہے۔ هران موی ر اگر کسی نے جمعہ کی نماز ظہر کی نیت سے ادا کی تو شیخین کے نزدیک ادا ہو جائے گی کیونکہ ان کا کے ایک جمعہ کے دن ظہری اصل ہے اور اصل کی نیت سے بدل ادا ہو جاتا ہے البتہ امام زفر کے نزدیک جمعہ کے دن جلدی میں ہے بدل نہیں ہے اس لئے ظہر کی نیت سے جمعہ ادا نہ ہوگا کیونکہ بدل کی نیت سے اصل ادا نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ عد جنب کتاب علیہ الرحمہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اصبح یہ ہے کہ نماز جمعہ ظہر کی نیت سے بھی ادا کر لی تو نماز جمعہ صیح ہو جائے گی مفصل جمعہ کی نماز کو جمعہ کی ہی نیت سے ادا کرنا چاہئے۔
And in skipping many, Friday is obligatory; whatever one begins is obligatory. Allama Hamawi's inclination is that Friday is reported. Also, before al-Mahmumah, the author had said that the obligatory time and the time of Zuhr are in the same ruling. But if someone made the intention of the obligatory time on Friday, then according to the two shaykhs, the intention of the obligatory time on Friday will be correct because according to them, on Friday, Friday prayer is the original, and Zuhr can become a substitute after Friday is missed. But if someone performed Friday prayer with the intention of Zuhr, then according to the two shaykhs it will be performed because according to them, on Friday, Zuhr is the original, and with the intention of the original, the substitute is performed. However, according to Imam Zufar, on Friday, Friday is the substitute, not the original, so Friday prayed with the intention of Zuhr will not be valid because the original is not performed with the intention of the substitute. Also, Sahib Kanz (Allah's mercy) says that the correct view is that if one performs Friday prayer with the intention of Zuhr, the Friday prayer will be valid. Preferably, Friday prayer should be performed with the intention of Friday.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi ruling on the intention for Friday prayer. It discusses whether Friday prayer is valid if one intends it as Zuhr. The author first notes that Friday is obligatory, then explains Allama Hamawi's view. The key dispute is between the two shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) and Imam Zufar. According to the two shaykhs, if one intends Friday prayer as the obligatory time (i.e., intending Friday), it is correct; but if one intends it as Zuhr, it is also valid because Zuhr is the original and Friday is its substitute on Friday. Imam Zufar holds the opposite: Friday is the substitute, so intending the original (Zuhr) for the substitute does not work. The author then cites a later scholar (possibly from Kanz al-Daqaiq) who supports the view that Friday prayer is valid even with Zuhr intention, but recommends intending Friday specifically.

Key Terms
تعيين (ta'yin): Specifying the exact type of act of worship in intention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the two shaykhs, if someone prays Friday prayer with the intention of Zuhr, is the prayer valid?
A) Yes, because Zuhr is the original and Friday is a substitute.
B) No, because intention must be for Friday.
C) Only if it is a make-up prayer.
D) It is invalid according to all scholars.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi view is that Friday prayer is valid even if intended as Zuhr, but it is recommended to specifically intend Friday.

Ruling on Intention Timing for Sick and Traveler in Ramadan
Rasm al-mufti rule on intention timing with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rasm al-mufti rule of takhfeef to determine the valid time for intention for sick and traveler in Ramadan fasts.

Core Idea
Takhfeef (leniency) overrides the general rule of night intention for sick and traveler.

This lesson examines a critical rasm al-mufti principle: when a rule causes hardship, the school may adopt a position of ease. The debate about intention timing for those with a valid excuse (sick, traveler) reveals how Hanafi jurists prioritize takhfeef over strict analogy. We will see how Abu Yusuf's view became the relied-upon fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Determine whether the requirement of night intention (niyyah min al-layl) applies equally to all fasting persons, including the sick and traveler, or whether they have a concession.
The base text made no distinction; the debate arises from this silence.
2
Understand Imam Zufar's objection
Imam Zufar analogized the sick/traveler's fast to qada (make-up) fasts, which require night intention. He argued that since fasting is not obligatory on them, it resembles qada.
Qiyas on qada is a plausible but contested analogy.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
The response rejects the qiyas as taghleez (imposing severity) whereas the underlying shar'i permission to not fast indicates takhfeef (leniency). Leniency is more appropriate.
This is a key application of the maxim 'al-mashaqqah tajlib al-taysir'.
4
Locate the mufta bihi position
Abu Yusuf held that intention after dawn but before midday (zawal) is valid. Later scholars like Hasan and the authors of Qunyah, Kashf Kabir, etc. adopted this. It becomes the relied-upon view.
The claim that Abu Hanifa and Muhammad required night intention is refuted; they also allowed after dawn.
5
Connect to other cases
The passage also discusses: (a) if one intends a nafl fast in Ramadan, it counts as Ramadan because it is more important; (b) if one vows a specific day and intends nafl, it becomes the vow per Abu Yusuf.
These illustrate the principle that the stronger obligation overrides the weaker intention.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
انہوں نے مریض ، مسافر اور مقیم کے درمیان کوئی تفصیل ذکر نہیں کی ہے۔ حیث قال فانه لا فرق بين الصحيح والمريض والمسافر والمقيم لانه لا يفصل فيما ذكرنا من الليل. امام زفر رحمہ اللہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مسافر اور مریض کے لئے رات سے ہی نیت کرنا ضروری ہے کیونکہ رمضان کے رنے کی ادائیگی ان پر واجب نہیں ہے تو یہ مثل قضا کے ہیں جیسے قضاء روزے کی ادائیگی کے لئے رات سے نیت کرنا ضروری ہے اسی طرح ان کے لئے رمضان کے روزے کی ادائیگی کے لئے رات سے ہی نیت کرنا ضروری ہے۔ امام زفر کے اس قول کو یہ کہہ کر رد کر دیا گیا ہے کہ اس میں تغلیظ ہے جب کہ مسافر اور مریض کے لئے مناسب تخفیف ہے۔ قنیہ میں نقل کیا گیا ہے کہ اگر مریض اور مسافر نے ماہ رمضان میں رات میں روزہ کی نیت نہ کی اور نصف النہار سے قبل روزہ کی نیت کر لی تو عندابی یوسف صحیح ہے۔ اور حسن نے بھی اسی کو اختیار کیا ہے۔ صاحب کشف کبیر فرماتے ہیں کہ عندالی یوسف کے ذکر سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ امام محمد اور امام ابی حنیفہ کے نزدیک مریض اور مسافر کے لئے رمضان کے روزہ کے لئے رات سے ہی نیت کرنا ضروری ہے حالانکہ ایسا نہیں ہے بلکہ ان کے نزدیک بھی اگر طلوع فجر کے بعد روزہ کی نیت یہ حضرات کرلیں تو رمضان کا روزہ ہو جائے گا۔ مبسوط نہا یہ اور ولوالجیہ میں اسی طرح مذکور ہے۔ وفي النفل روايتان: اگر کسی نے رمضان کے ماہ میں نقل کی نیت سے روزہ رکھا تو اس میں دور وایتیں ہیں۔ (۱) نفل کا روزہ ہوگا۔ (۲) رمضان کا شمار ہوگا اور یہی صحیح ہے۔ تمر تاشی کی جامع صغیر کی شرح میں ہے کہ اگر مسافر نے رمضان کے ماہ میں نفلی روزہ رکھا تو ان سے دو روایتوں میں سے اصح یہ ہے کہ رمضان کا روزہ ہوگا اس لئے کہ رمضان کا روز ہ زیادہ اہم ہے۔ امام کرتی نے مریض کو بھی اسی پر محمول کیا ہے، ایک قول یہ ہے کہ چاہے وہ جس کی نیت کرے رمضان ہی کا روزہ ہوگا بالاتفاق اس لئے کہ مریض کو روزہ نہ رکھنے کی اجازت بجز کی وجہ سے تھی اور روزہ رکھنے سے یہ معلوم ہو گیا کہ وہ عاجز نہیں ہے۔ اور مسافر کے حق میں صحیح سفر ہے اور وہ اب بھی موجود ہے۔ اور اس میں ایک مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے متعین دن کے روزہ رکھنے کی نذر مانی اور اس دن میں نفل کی نیت سے روزہ رکھا تو امام ابو یوسف کی روایت یہ ہے کہ نذر کا روزہ ہوگا اور اگر کسی واجب آخر کی نیت کی تو اس کی نیت کے مطابق روزہ ہو گا۔ اس لئے کہ نفل اس کے لئے مشروع ہے اور فرض اس پر مشروع ہے اور بندہ شریعت کی طرف سے اپنے اوپر عائد کردہ وقت کو تبدیل کرنے کا اختیار نہیں رکھتا۔
They did not mention any detail between sick, traveler and resident. As he said: there is no difference between healthy and sick, traveler and resident because he does not differentiate [regarding] what we mentioned of the night. Imam Zufar (may Allah have mercy on him) says that it is necessary for the traveler and sick to intend from the night because performing the Ramadan fast is not obligatory upon them, so they are like qada; just as for performing a qada fast, intention from the night is necessary, similarly for them, for performing the Ramadan fast, intention from the night is necessary. Imam Zufar's statement is rejected by saying that it involves severity while for the traveler and sick, suitable leniency is appropriate. In Qunyah it is reported that if the sick and traveler did not intend the fast at night in the month of Ramadan and intended before midday, then according to Abu Yusuf it is valid, and Hasan also adopted this. The author of Kashf Kabir says that from the mention of 'according to Abu Yusuf' it appears that according to Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Hanifa, it is necessary for the sick and traveler to intend the Ramadan fast from the night, although it is not so; rather, according to them also, if they intend the fast after dawn, the Ramadan fast will be valid. In Mabsut, Nahayah and Walwaljiyyah it is similarly mentioned. And regarding nafl, there are two narrations: if someone intended a nafl fast in Ramadan, then there are two narrations: (1) it will be a nafl fast; (2) it will count as Ramadan, and this is correct. In the commentary of Jami' al-Saghir by Tamartashi, it is stated that if a traveler keeps a nafl fast in Ramadan, then among the two narrations, the more correct is that it will be a Ramadan fast because the Ramadan fast is more important. Imam Karti has applied the same to the sick. One statement is that whatever he intends, it will definitely be a Ramadan fast by consensus, because the sick were given permission not to fast due to inability, and by fasting it becomes clear that he is not incapable. And regarding the traveler, his travel is valid and still present. And in this, there is an issue: if someone vowed to fast a specific day and on that day intended a nafl fast, then according to Abu Yusuf, it will be the vowa fast; and if he intended another obligatory fast, then it will be according to his intention. Because nafl is prescribed for him and obligatory is prescribed upon him, and the servant does not have the authority to change the time imposed upon him by the Shariah.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage is a rasm rule (methodological ruling) from the Hanafi school regarding the timing of intention (niyyah) for Ramadan fasts specifically for sick persons and travelers. The discussion begins by noting that the base text made no distinction between the healthy resident and the sick/traveler in requiring intention from the night. Imam Zufar argues that sick and traveler must intend from night because their fast is like qada (make-up), which requires pre-dawn intention. The rebuttal states this is too harsh (taghleez) whereas leniency (takhfeef) is appropriate for them. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that if they intend after dawn but before midday, it is valid according to Abu Yusuf and Hasan. The claim that Abu Hanifa and Muhammad required night intention is refuted; they also allow after dawn. Then the passage discusses the issue of nafl intention in Ramadan: the correct view is that it counts as Ramadan because Ramadan is more important. For a vow (nazr) on a specific day, if one intends nafl, it becomes the vow according to Abu Yusuf, because the servant cannot override the time imposed by Shariah. The key point is that the mufti should follow the opinion of ease for sick and traveler, while the default for Ramadan is that it overrides other intentions.

Key Terms
نیت (niyyah): Intention (in the heart) to perform a specific act of worship
مریض (marid): Sick person who is permitted to not fast due to illness
مسافر (musafir): Traveler who is permitted to not fast due to travel

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, when can a sick person or traveler in Ramadan make the intention to fast?
A) Only before dawn (suhur time)
B) Before midday (zawal) if they did not intend at night
C) At any time even after midday
D) They cannot fast because it is not obligatory

Key Takeaway
For sick and traveler, the mufta bihi is that intention before midday suffices for a valid Ramadan fast, based on the principle of takhfeef.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
10 min
Ta'yin in Qada of Prayers and Fasts
Explaining when specification is needed in making up missed acts of worship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule of ta'yin in qada to determine when specification is required for valid intention.

Core Idea
Specification is only needed when different types of obligations overlap; same type does not need specification.

When making up missed prayers and fasts, you may wonder whether you need to specify exactly which day or year you are intending. This passage from the Hanafi tradition clarifies the rule: specification (ta'yin) depends on whether the missed acts are of the same type (jins) or different. Understanding this distinction is crucial for a mufti advising on the validity of qada.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling on ta'yin in qada
Read the passage and extract the general principle: specification is not required when the missed acts are of the same type (e.g., days from one Ramadan), but is required when they are of different types (e.g., days from two different Ramadans, or between Zuhr and Asr prayers).
The key term is 'jins' (type).
2
Distinguish between fasts and prayers
Note that for fasts, the ruling differs based on whether the missed days are from one Ramadan or multiple Ramadans. For prayers, even a single missed prayer requires specification of the prayer and its day because each prayer is a distinct type.
Prayers are more specific: each prayer (Zuhr, Asr, etc.) is a separate jins.
3
Apply the concession for ease
The passage provides a practical solution (mukhlis) for someone who does not know the exact dates: intending the 'first Zuhr upon me' or 'last Zuhr upon me' is valid, and sequential assumption validates the earlier ones.
This concession is for ease, not a change in the rule.
4
Evaluate the ikhtilaf
The passage mentions two opinions: the 'asah' (most sound) requiring ta'yin for different types, and the muhtar (preferred) that even two Ramadans do not need specification. Understand why the mufta bihi is the 'asah'.
The author did not give fatwa on the muhtar because al-Zayla'i deemed it unsound.
5
Prepare a fatwa response
Based on the mufta bihi, formulate a clear ruling: specification is required when making up missed acts of different types; not required when same type. Provide the reasoning and acknowledge the concession for ease when exact dates are unknown.
This is the operative ruling for issuing fatwa.

وَأَمَّا إِذَا كَثُرَتِ الْفَوَائِتُ، فَاخْتَلَفُوا فِي إِشْتِرَاطِ التَّعْيِينِ لِتَمْيِيزِ الْفُرُوضِ الْمُتَّحِدَةِ مِنْ جنسٍ وَاحِدٍ، وَالأَصَحُ أَنَّهُ إِنْ كَانَ عَلَيْهِ قَضَاءُ يَوْمِ مِنْ رَمَضَانَ وَاحِدٍ فَصَامَ يَوْمَا نَاوِيَا عَنْهُ وَلَكِنْ لَمْ يُعَيِّنْ أَنَّهُ صَائِمٌ عَنْ يَوْمٍ كَذَا، فَإِنَّهُ يَجُوْزُ، وَلَا يَجُوْزُ فِي رَمَضَانَيْنِ مَالَمْ يُعَيِّنْ أَنَّهُ صَائِمٌ عَنْ رَمَضَانَ سَنَةٍ كَذَا. وَلَوْ كَانَتِ الْفَوَاتُ كَثِيرَةً فَاشْتَغَلَ بِالْقَضَاءِ يَحْتَاجُ إِلَى تَعْيِينِ الظُّهْرِ أَوِ الْعَصْرِ أَوْ نَحْوِهَا وَيَنْوِي أَيْضاً ظُهْرَ يَوْمِ كَذَا وَعَصْرَ يَوْمِ كَذَا فَإِذَا أَرَادَ تَسْهِيلَ الْأَمْرِ يَنْوِي أَوَّلَ ظُهْرٍ عَلَيْهِ أَوْ آخِرَ ظُهْرٍ عَلَيْهِ وَإِذَا نَوَى الْأَوَّلَ وَصَلَّى فِيمَا يَلِيهِ يَصِيرُ أَوَّلًا. وَأَمَّا قَضَاءُ الصَّلَاةِ : فَلَا يَجُوزُ مَالَمْ يُعَيِّنِ الصَّلَاةَ وَيَوْمَهَا، بِأَنْ يُعَيِّنْ ظُهْرَ يَوْمٍ كَذَا، وَلَوْ نَوَى أَوَّلَ ظُهْرٍ عَلَيْهِ، أَوْ آخِرَ ظُهْرٍ عَلَيْهِ جَازَ، وَهَذَا هُوَ الْمَخْلِصُ لِمَنْ لَّمْ يَعْرِفِ الْأَوْقَاتِ الْفَائِتَةَ، أَوِ اشْتَبَهَتْ عَلَيْهِ، أَوْ أَرَادَ التَّسْهِيلَ عَلَى نَفْسِهِ.
As for when missed acts are numerous, they differed concerning the requirement of specification to distinguish identical obligations of one type. The most sound is that if one has to make up a day from one Ramadan and he fasted a day intending it but did not specify that he is fasting for such-and-such a day, then it is permissible. And it is not permissible in two Ramadans unless he specifies that he is fasting for the Ramadan of such-and-such a year. And when missed acts are many and he occupies himself with making up, he needs to specify the prayer (Zuhr, Asr, or similar) and also intends Zuhr of such-and-such a day and Asr of such-and-such a day. But if he wants to ease the matter, he intends the first Zuhr upon him or the last Zuhr upon him. And if he intends the first and prays the next ones, the first becomes [valid]. As for making up prayer: it is not valid unless he specifies the prayer and its day, such that he specifies Zuhr of such-and-such a day. And if he intends the first Zuhr upon him or the last Zuhr upon him, it is valid. And this is the way out for one who does not know the missed times, or is confused about them, or wants ease for himself.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage is a legal ruling on the requirement of specification (ta'yin) in making up missed obligatory prayers and fasts. The author begins with the case of fasting: when only one Ramadan is missed, specifying the exact day is not required because all days of the same Ramadan are of the same type (jins). However, if days from two different Ramadans are missed, specification of the year is necessary because the types differ. For prayers, the ruling is stricter: even for a single missed prayer, both the prayer and its day must be specified because each prayer (e.g., Zuhr, Asr) is a different type. To facilitate the one who does not know the exact dates, the author allows intending the first or last of a particular missed prayer type, sequential assumption then validates the earlier ones. This is a practical concession (mukhlis) for ease.

Key Terms
تعيين (ta'yin): Specification of the exact type or occasion of an act of worship in the intention.
جنس (jins): Type or category of obligation; e.g., Zuhr prayer vs. Asr prayer, or Ramadan of one year vs. another.
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed obligatory act of worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the 'asah' opinion in this passage, when must a person specify the year when making up missed fasts?
A) When fasting for one missed day from one Ramadan
B) When fasting for missed days from two different Ramadans
C) When fasting for any missed day regardless of Ramadan
D) Specification of year is never required in qada fasts

Key Takeaway
Specification (ta'yin) in qada is required only when different types of obligations are involved; same-type obligations do not require it.

Ta'yin in Qada' Fasts: The Ruling and the Mukhtar
Ruling on ta'yin for qada' fasts from two Ramadans

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida 'ind ikhtilaf al-ajnas la budda min al-tamyiz to determine when specification is required in qada' fasts, and identify the mufta bihi position in the school.

Core Idea
When species differ, distinction is necessary, but the preferred view in later Hanafiyya is that ta'yin is not required.

This passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir illustrates a tension between a general qawida and the actual fatwa practice. The author states that specification is required for qada' fasts from two Ramadans because the months are different species. However, the commentary reveals that this is not the mukhtar (preferred) view; later authorities hold that specification is not necessary, though it remains better. Understanding this layered ruling is a critical part of the mufti's training.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the qawida
Read the first part of the passage: the author states that ta'yin is required because the cause (sabab) differs, making the species distinct. This invokes the qawida: 'When species differ, distinction is necessary.'
The qawida is a wusta (intermediate) maxim.
2
Recognize the disagreement
Note the commentary: Allamah Jumu'i and others report that the mukhtar view in the madhhab is that specification is not required. The author of al-Ashbah transmitted the opposite view out of deference to Zayla'i.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Determine the mufta bihi
The passage indicates that the later Hanafi position (mukhtar) is that ta'yin is not necessary, although it is recommended. This is the operative view for fatwa today.
Many muftis follow the mukhtar view.
4
Understand the thamarah
The practical consequence: a person with qada' fasts from two Ramadans need not specify which month each fast belongs to in the intention; the general intention to make up fasts suffices.
Specifying is still better for ihtiyat.
5
Apply the qawida with its istithna'
Although the qawida says distinction is necessary, the mukhtar view effectively creates an exception: because the essential obligation (qada') is of the same genus (fasting), the difference in cause does not necessitate specification.
This shows the importance of consulting the rasm al-mufti literature.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عليه قضاء يومين من رمضانين يحتاج الى التعيين (تاتار خانیه ج ۱ ص ۴۱۹) شخص پر دور مضان کے دو روزوں کی قضاء ہے تو اب جب تک وہ نیت کے وقت سال کے ساتھ رمضان کے مہینہ کی تعین نہ کرے گا اس وقت اس کے روزے بیچ نہیں ہوں گے کیونکہ روزہ کا سبب مہینہ ہے اور وہ یہاں دونوں میں الگ الگ ہیں لہذا دونوں کی جنس بھی الگ الگ ہوئی اور جب جنس الگ الگ ہے تو ا۔ یہ تین لازم ہے۔ علامہ جموعی فرماتے ہیں گذشتہ مسئلہ میں صاحب کتاب نے مختار قول کے خلاف نقل کیا ہے بزاز یہ اور اس کے علاوہ میں مذکور ہے کہ اگر کسی پر دور مضان کے روزے ہوں تو مختار مذہب کے مطابق تعیین ضروری نہیں ہے اگر چہ تعیین نیت افضل ہے۔ علامہ حموی فرماتے ہیں کہ عنقریب فتح القدیر کے حوالہ سے دوسرے صفحہ پر آرہا ہے کہ جائز ہے اگر چہ متعین نہ کیا ہو یا قول کے مطابق ، مصنف نے مختار پر فتویٰ نہیں دیا اس لئے کہ علامہ زیلعی نے دور مضان کے روزوں کو بدونِ تعین صحیح قرار نہیں دیا نیز صاحب اشباہ کا بیان کردہ مسئلہ قاعدہ مذکورہ کے موافق ہے۔
Upon him is the qada of two days from two Ramadans; it requires specification (Tatar Khaniya vol. 1 p. 419). A person has the qada of two fasts from two Ramadans; now as long as he does not specify the month of Ramadan along with the year at the time of intention, his fasts will not be valid because the cause of the fast is the month, and they are separate here, so their species also become separate. And when the species is separate, then it is necessary to distinguish. Allamah Jumu'i says: In the previous issue, the author of the book has transmitted against the preferred view. In Bazzaziyyah and others, it is mentioned that if a person has fasts from two Ramadans, then according to the preferred view, specification is not necessary, although specifying the intention is better. Allamah Hamawi says: Soon in the second page with reference to Fath al-Qadir, it is coming that it is permissible even if he did not specify; or according to the saying, the author did not give a fatwa on the preferred view because Allamah Zayla'i did not deem the fasts of two Ramadans valid without specification, and also the issue stated by the author of al-Ashbah is in accordance with the mentioned rule.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on specifying the month when making up missed fasts from two different Ramadans. The author of the base text (likely Al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir) states that specification is required because the cause (sabab) for each fast is a distinct month, making the species (jins) different. When species differ, distinction (tamyiz) is necessary. However, the commentary notes that this is not the preferred (mukhtar) view in the madhhab; many later authorities hold that specification is not necessary, though it is better. The author of al-Ashbah did not give fatwa on the preferred view due to opposition from Zayla'i, but the passage aligns with the qawida that different species require distinction.

Key Terms
تعيين (ta'yin): Specification of the particular obligation (month, day, etc.) in intention.
جنس (jins): Species or category of obligation based on its cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the final fatwa (mufta bihi) regarding specification of the month in qada' fasts from two Ramadans?
A) Specification is fard (obligatory).
B) Specification is mustahabb (recommended) but not required.
C) Specification invalidates the fast if done.
D) The school has no settled view.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the mufta bihi for qada' fasts from multiple Ramadans is that ta'yin is not required, though it is better to specify; this demonstrates how later tarjih may restrict a general qawida.

Specification in Qada Prayers: Ruling, Easy Method, and Scholarly Critique
Ruling on ta'yin for qada prayers with critical refinement from al-Muhit and Ibn Nujaym

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi position on ta'yin for qada prayers, distinguish the mufta bihi from the minority view, and apply the qawida of species distinction.

Core Idea
Specify prayer and day for qada, or intend 'first/last'; the relied view requires ta'yin.

This passage examines the necessity of specifying the particular prayer and its day when making up missed prayers. While the basic ruling insists on exact specification, the Hanafi school provides an easy method for those with many missed prayers. A dissenting view in al-Muhit argues against the need for ta'yin, but the relied-upon position maintains it based on the essential difference between prayer species.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and basic ruling
The matn states: qada of prayer is not permissible unless one specifies the prayer and its day (e.g., Zuhr of such-and-such day). This is the default ruling.
This applies when multiple prayers are due.
2
Understand the easy method
If one intends 'first Zuhr upon me' or 'last Zuhr upon me', it is valid. This is the ’mukhlis‘ (way out) for those who don't know exact times or want ease.
This method is for numerous missed prayers.
3
Recognize the alternative view from al-Muhit
Al-Muhit argues that ta'yin is not inherently required; it is only needed to maintain order (tartib). If order drops (due to multitude), mere intention of 'Zuhr' suffices without day.
This view separates the obligation of the prayer from the obligation of order.
4
Analyze the critique by Ibn Nujaym
Ibn Nujaym finds the al-Muhit view problematic because it abandons the agreed-upon rule that distinction is made for different species. Prayers are different species due to different causes, so ta'yin is essential.
The critique is based on a qawida (principle) of species distinction.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is that of Qadi Khan and others: ta'yin is required. However, the easy method (first/last) is permissible for those with many missed prayers.
Ibn Nujaym's rejection of al-Muhit is accepted, so the school's position is settled.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا قَضَاءُ الصَّلوةِ : فَلَا يَجُوزُ مَالَمْ يُعَيِّنِ الصَّلَاةَ وَيَوْمَهَا، بِأَنْ يُعَيِّنْ ظُهْرَ يَوْمٍ كَذَا، وَلَوْ نوى أوَّلَ ظُهرٍ عَلَيْهِ، أَوْ آخِرَ ظُهْرِ عَلَيْهِ جَازَ، وَهَذَا هُوَ الْمَخْلِصُ لِمَنْ لَّمْ يَعْرِفِ الأوْقَاتِ الْفَائِتَةَ، أَوْ إِشْتَبَهَتْ عَلَيْهِ، أو أرَادَ التَّسْهِيْلَ عَلَى نَفْسِهِ. تشریح ادا نماز کی تعیین کے لئے صرف اتنا کافی ہے کہ آج کی ظہر یا اس وقت کی ظہر ادا کر رہا ہوں جب کہ قضاء نماز کی ادائیگی کے لئے وقت اور تاریخ دونوں کی تعیین ضروری ہے کیونکہ متعدد نمازوں کی جنس الگ الگ ہے لیکن یہ اس وقت ہے جبکہ قضاء نمازیں متعدد ہوں اور نہ اگر کسی کے ذمہ میں صرف ایک ہی ظہر کی نماز ہو تو صرف اتنا کہنا کافی ہے کہ ظہر کی چھوٹی ہوئی نماز ادا کر رہا ہوں اگر چہا اسے یہ بھی معلوم نہ ہو کہ وہ ظہر کی نماز کون سے دن کی ہے ادنی تعیین کافی ہے جیسا کہ ابن امیر حاج العلمی کی شرح المنیۃ میں ہے ولو كانت الفوائت كثيرة فاشتغل بالقضاء يحتاج الى تعيين الظهر أو العصر او نحوهما وينوى ايضاً ظهر يوم كذا وعصر يوم كذا . (تاتار خانيه ج ۱ ص / ۷۳۹) ولونوی اول ظهر :علیه اگر کسی کی لمبی مدت کی نمازیں قضاء ہوں تو ان کو ادا کرتے وقت نیت کا آسان طریقہ یہ ہے کہ نیت کرے کہ میں مثلاً قضاء شدہ ظہر کی نمازوں میں پہلی ظہر یا آخری ظہر ادا کر رہا ہوں ہر قضاء نماز میں اسی طرح نیت کرتا رہے تو اسی نیت سے اس کی قضاء نمازیں ادا ہوتی رہیں گی یہ طریقہ ان لوگوں کے لئے مفید ہے جن کو فوت شدہ نمازوں کی تعداد معلوم نہ ہوں یہ چھوٹی ہوئی نمازوں میں اشتباہ پیدا ہو جائے یا آسمانی کے مقصد سے اس طرح سے نیت کرے تو اس طرح کی تعیین کافی ہے۔ وَذَكَرَ فِي الْمُحِيْطِ : أَنَّ نِيَّةَ التَّعْمِيْنِ فِى الصَّلَاةِ لَمْ تُشْتَرَطُ بِااعْتِبَارِ أَنَّ الْوَاجِبَ مُخْتَلِفٌ مُتَعَدِدٌ، بَلْ بِاعْتِبَارِ أَنَّ مُرَاعَاةَ التَّرْتِيْبِ وَاجِبٌ عَلَيْهِ، وَلَا يُمْكِنُهُ مُرَاعَاةُ التَّرْتِيبِ إِلَّا بَنية النَّعْيَيْنِ حَتَّى لَوْسَقَطَ التَّرْتِيْبُ بِكَثْرَةِ الْفَوَائِتِ تَكْفِيْهِ نِيَّةُ الظُّهْرِ لَا غَيْرَ، وَهَذَا مُشْكِل وَمَا ذَكَرَهُ أَصْحَابُنَا كَقَاضِيْ خَانٍ وَغَيْرِهِ خِلَافُهُ، وَهُوَ الْمُعْتَمَدُ كَذَا فِي النَّبِيِّنِ. ترجمہ: اور جیب میں ذکرکیا گیا ہے کہ نمازمیں تعین کی نیت شرط نہیں ہے اس اعتبار سے کہ واجب مختلف شعور ہے بلکہ اس اعتبار سے کہ ترتیب کی رعایت اس پر واجب ہے اور ترتیب کی رعایت بدون نیت تعین ممکن نہیں ہے تھی کہ کثرت فوائت کی وجہ سے اگر ترتیب ساقط ہو جائے تو ظہر کی نیت کافی ہے نہ کہ اس کے علاوہ اور یہ مشکل ہے اور جو ہمارے اصحاب نے ذکر کیا ہے جیسے قاضی خاں وغیرہ وہ اس کے خلاف ہے اور یہی قابل اعتماد ہے تبیین میں اسی طرح ہے۔ تشریح : علامه ابن نجیم المصری فرماتے ہیں کہ محیط میں یہ ذکر کیا گیا ہے کہ نیت کی تعین نماز میں اس کے شرط نہیں ہے کہ واجب مختلف اور متعدد ہے بلکہ اس اعتبار سے ہے کہ مصلی پر ترتیب کی رعایت رکھنا واجب ہے اور تعیین کی نیت کے بغیر ترتیب کی رعایت رکھنا ممکن نہیں لہذا اگر کثرت فوائت کی وجہ سے ترتیب ساقط ہو جائے تو صرف ظہر کی نیت اس کے لئے کافی ہوگی یوم وغیرہ کی نیت کی ضرورت نہ ہوگی ۔ علامہ ابن نجیم المصری فرماتے ہیں کہ صاحب محیط کی یہ تشریح مشکل ہے اور وجہ اشکال یہ ہے کہ اس بات کو تلیم کرنے کی صورت میں فقہاء کا وہ قاعدہ ختم ہو جاتا ہے جس پر انہوں نے اتفاق کیا ہے وہ یہ کہ تین اجناس کی تمیز ے لئے ہوتی ہے اور تمام نمازیں مختلف اجناس کے قبیل سے ہیں کیونکہ اسباب مختلف ہیں۔ علامہ فرماتے ہیں کہ ہمارے اصحاب مثلاً قاضی خاں وغیرہ نے اس سلسلہ میں جو بات ذکر کی ہے وہ اگر چان کے خلاف ہے لیکن وہی معتمد ہے۔
And as for the qada of prayer: it is not permissible until he specifies the prayer and its day, by specifying the Zuhr of such-and-such a day. And if he intends 'the first Zuhr upon him' or 'the last Zuhr upon him,' it is permissible. And this is the way out for one who does not know the times of the missed prayers, or they are confused for him, or he wants to make it easy for himself. Clarification: For specifying an ada prayer, it is sufficient to say 'I am performing today's Zuhr' or 'this time's Zuhr,' whereas for performing qada prayer, specification of both time and date is necessary because the species of multiple prayers are different. But this is when the qada prayers are multiple; if a person has only one Zuhr prayer due, it is sufficient to say 'I am performing the missed Zuhr prayer' even if he does not know which day it was; minimal specification is sufficient, as in Sharh al-Munya by Ibn Amir Hajj al-Halabi: 'And if the missed prayers are many, and he busies himself with qada, he needs to specify Zuhr or Asr or the like, and he also intends 'Zuhr of such a day' and 'Asr of such a day.' (Tatar Khaniya vol. 1 p. 739). And if he intends 'first Zuhr upon him,' if a person has qada of prayers for a long period, then at the time of performing them, an easy method is to intend, for example, 'I am performing the first Zuhr of the missed Zuhr prayers' or 'the last Zuhr.' By intending similarly in each qada prayer, his qada prayers will be performed with that intention. This method is beneficial for those who do not know the number of missed prayers, or there is confusion about them, or he intends for the sake of ease; such specification is sufficient. And it is mentioned in al-Muhit that the intention of specification in prayer is not required because the obligation is different and multiple, but rather because observing the order is obligatory upon him, and it is not possible for him to observe the order except by an intention of specification. So if the order drops due to multitude of missed prayers, the intention of 'Zuhr' alone suffices, not otherwise. And this is problematic, and what our companions like Qadi Khan and others have mentioned is contrary to it, and it is the relied-upon view. Thus in al-Tabyin. Translation: And it is mentioned in al-Muhit that the intention of specification in prayer is not required because the obligation is different and multiple, but rather because observing the order is obligatory upon him, and it is not possible to observe order without the intention of specification. So if the order drops due to multitude of missed prayers, then the intention of 'Zuhr' alone suffices, no need for specifying the day. Allamah Ibn Nujaym al-Misri says: This explanation from the author of al-Muhit is problematic, and the reason for the problem is that by adopting this view, the rule upon which the jurists have agreed—that distinction is made for the sake of different species—would be eliminated, because all prayers are from different species due to different causes. Allamah says: What our companions like Qadi Khan and others have mentioned in this regard is contrary to it, but it is the relied-upon view.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage discusses the necessity of specification (ta'yin) when performing qada prayers. The author of the matn states that for qada, the prayer and its day must be specified, but if one intends the 'first' or 'last' of a type (e.g., first Zuhr due), it suffices. The commentary then discusses the opinion from al-Muhit, which argues that specification is not required because the obligation (wajib) is the prayer itself, not its time; the need for specification arises only from the obligation to maintain order (tartib). If order drops, mere intention of 'Zuhr' suffices. Ibn Nujaym criticizes this, stating that it contradicts the agreed-upon rule that distinction is necessary when species differ, and all prayers are different species. The relied-upon view in the madhhab is that specification is required, as held by Qadi Khan and others.

Key Terms
تعيين (ta'yin): Specification of the particular prayer and its day in intention.
ترتيب (tartib): The order in which missed prayers must be made up.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view in the Hanafi madhhab, what is required when a person has many missed prayers to make up?
A) Specifying only the prayer type (e.g., Zuhr) without the day.
B) Specifying both the prayer and the day (e.g., Zuhr of a specific day).
C) Specifying only the time of day (e.g., first or last).
D) No specification is required at all.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi requires ta'yin in qada prayers, but minimal specification like 'first Zuhr' is acceptable; the al-Muhit view is not the relied-upon position.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
10 min
Effect of Error in Specification (Ta'yin) on Acts of Worship and Testimony
Rasm al-mufti rule: error in non-essential specification does not harm, but error in essential specification does.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule on error in specification (ta'yin) to determine the validity of acts of worship and testimony.

Core Idea
Error in non-essential details is excused; error in the essence of an act invalidates it.

This passage from Sharah al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair presents a key principle for muftis: whether an error in specifying the nature or details of an act affects its validity. The answer depends on whether the specification is legally required. Through examples from prayer, testimony, and congregational prayer, the author illustrates when the error is overlooked and when it breaks the act. This rule is essential for issuing fatwas on the validity of worship and legal testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule
Read the first part of the passage to extract the overarching principle: error in what does not require specification does not harm, and error in what requires specification does harm. Note that this is a rasm al-mufti rule.
The rule is stated explicitly at the beginning of the passage and repeated in the commentary.
2
Examine the Non-Harmful Cases
Focus on the first set of examples: mistaking ada for qada in prayer, and witnesses erring on the color of a stolen animal. For each, note why specification is not required and therefore the error does not invalidate.
For ada/qada, the essence of prayer is captured; for color, it is non-essential to the claim.
3
Examine the Harmful Cases
Study the second set: error between fasting and prayer, between Zuhr and Asr, and specifying a named imam (e.g., intending Zaid when it is 'Amr). Identify that specification is essential because the act's identity changes.
The imam case shows that if the follower specifies a name, error harms; if generic intention, not.
4
Apply the Rule to New Scenarios
Using the principle, analyze a new case: e.g., a person intends to pray Maghrib but mistakenly intends Isha. Determine if specification is required and thus whether the prayer is valid.
Since Maghrib and Isha are distinct obligatory prayers, specification is required, so error invalidates.

The color of the animal, so they mentioned a color, then they testified at the time of claim and mentioned another color: it is accepted, because contradiction in what is not needed does not harm. End. Translation: And among these are two cases: when he specifies it as ada then it becomes apparent that the time has passed, or he specifies it as qada then it becomes apparent that time remains. And derived from it: when a witness mentions something unnecessary and errs in it, it is not harmful. And Bazzaziyyah [?] said to us: If the judge asked them about the color of the animal, and they mentioned one color, then at the time of claim they testified and mentioned another color, the testimony is accepted because contradiction in unnecessary matters is not harmful. The words of Bazzaziyyah are complete. Explanation: In ada and qada prayer, specifying ada or qada is not required. But if error occurs in specifying ada or qada, it is not harmful. For example, a person was praying an ada prayer and intended qada, or was praying qada and intended ada, his prayer is valid because specifying ada or qada was not obligatory upon him, so the error is not harmful. And if a man intends to pray the noon prayer of his day, and he thinks that the time of noon has not gone out, but the time has gone out, and he intends the noon of the day, it is permissible because when the time went out, the noon of the day became established in his liability, so when he intends the noon of the day, he has intended what is upon him, except that he performed qada of what is upon him with the intention of ada, and performing qada of what is upon him with the intention of ada is permissible (Bazzaziyyah, p. 82/83). And upon this is the witness: In testimony, if there is something not needed and the witnesses err in it, this error is not a hindrance to accepting the testimony. For example, the judge asked the witnesses about the color of the animal, so they said black or another, and when asked at the time of claim they told a different color, this does not affect the testimony because specification of color is not needed; absolute testimony about the animal is sufficient. And if the judge asks about the color... up to his statement: contradiction in what is not needed does not harm. Its origin is in al-Jami' al-Saghir: disagreement about the color of the animal in a claim of theft: it is accepted according to him because it is like remaining silent about mentioning the color. Bazzaziyyah on the margin of al-Hindiyya, vol. 5, p. 351. And as for that in which specification is required, error from fasting to prayer and vice versa, and from noon prayer to afternoon prayer, then it is harmful. Translation: And as for matters in which specification is a condition, such as error in place of fasting by prayer or vice versa, and error in noon prayer instead of afternoon, then it is harmful. Explanation: Matters in which specification is a condition: if someone errs when specifying, then it is harmful, such as someone specified prayer instead of fasting or fasting instead of prayer, or specified noon prayer instead of afternoon prayer, then this error is harmful for him, because for the validity of fasting and for the substitution of each prayer, specification is necessary. Therefore, when error occurred in the very essence of the act, it will be considered, and the prayer or fasting will not be valid. And from that is the case when he intends to follow Zaid, and then it turns out he is 'Amr. And it is better that he not specify the imam when there is a large congregation, lest it become apparent that he is other than the specified one, which is not permissible. So it is appropriate that he intends the one standing in the niche, whoever it may be, even if it does not occur to his mind that it is Zaid or 'Amr, his following is permissible. And if he intends to follow the imam standing, while he sees that it is Zaid, but it is 'Amr, his following is valid because consideration is for what he intended, not what he saw, and he intended to follow the imam. Translation: And from this category is the case when he intended to follow Zaid, and it turned out he was 'Amr. And it is better that he not specify the imam when congregation is large, lest his being other than specified become apparent, which is not permissible. So it is appropriate that he intend the one standing in the niche, whoever it may be, and even if it does not cross his mind that he is Zaid or 'Amr, his following is permissible. And if he intended to follow the imam standing, while he sees that he is Zaid, and he is 'Amr, his following is valid because consideration is for what he intended, not what he saw, and he intended to follow the imam. Explanation: This issue is also related to the previous issue. If a follower intended Zaid, later it became known that he was not Zaid but 'Amr, then in this case too, error in specification is harmful because intention is considered, and he intended to follow Zaid. And if he said 'I follow Zaid' or intended to follow, and it turned out he is 'Amr, his following is not correct because consideration is for what he intended, and he intended to follow Zaid. (Khaaniyah on margin of al-Hindiyya, vol. 1, p. 83). So the better way is to intend only the imam himself, whoever he may be, so that one does not suffer loss due to error in specification. And it is appropriate for the follower, if the people are many, not to specify the imam, but to say: 'I follow the imam standing in this niche; as the imam prays, I pray that prayer' (Khaaniyah on margin of al-Hindiyya, vol. 1, p. 84). And if he intends to follow the imam standing, and he sees that he is Zaid, then he turns out to be 'Amr, the following is valid, and his mistaken thought has no effect.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage from Sharah Al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair discusses a rasm al-mufti rule: The effect of error in specification (ta'yin) in acts of worship and legal testimony. The author first states a general principle: error in what does not require specification does not harm; error in what requires specification does harm. He then provides several furuat (applications). The first application concerns the distinction between ada (on-time) and qada (make-up) in prayer. In Hanafi fiqh, specifying whether a prayer is ada or qada is not a condition for validity. Therefore, if a person mistakenly intends qada when actually performing ada, or vice versa, the prayer remains valid. The author cites a specific case from al-Bazzaziyya: if a person intends to pray the noon prayer of the day, thinking the time has not passed, but it has passed, the prayer is valid as qada because the obligation has already entered his liability. The second application is in testimony. If a witness makes an error in an unnecessary detail, such as the color of a stolen animal, the testimony is still accepted because the color is not essential to the claim. The author references al-Jami' al-Saghir and al-Hindiyya. The third application concerns following an imam in congregational prayer. If a follower intends to follow a specific person (e.g., Zaid) but it turns out to be 'Amr, the prayer is invalid if he specified Zaid by name. However, if he intends simply 'the imam standing in the niche' without naming, and he turns out to be someone else, the prayer is valid. The better practice, as noted, is to avoid specifying the imam's name, especially in large congregations. The passage emphasizes that the guiding rule is that error in non-essential specification is excused, but error in essential specification invalidates the act. This is a key principle for muftis when evaluating the validity of worship and testimony.

Key Terms
تعيين (ta'yin): Specification of the particular act, time, or person in intention or utterance.
خطأ (khata): Error or mistake in the specification of something.
ادا وقضاء (ada wa qada): Ada: performing an act in its prescribed time; Qada: performing it after its time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, if a person intending to pray Zuhr mistakenly thinks the time has not passed but it actually has, and he intends 'Zuhr of today', what is the ruling?
A) The prayer is invalid because he intended ada when it was due as qada.
B) The prayer is valid as qada because the obligation was established and he intended what is upon him.
C) The prayer is invalid because he did not specify correctly.
D) The prayer is valid as nafl (supererogatory) because of the error.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, error in specification only invalidates an act if the specification is legally required; otherwise, the act remains valid.

Intending Contrary to Actual Performance: The Jumu'ah Exception (Rasm al-Mufti)
Rule that intention must match actual prayer with intra-Hanafi dispute on Jumu'ah latecomers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general Hanafi rule on intending contrary to actual prayer and identify the mufta bihi position regarding the reported Jumu'ah exception.

Core Idea
You cannot intend something different from what you are praying — and the Jumu'ah exception is rejected in the relied-upon madhhab.

This lesson examines a foundational rule of niyyah: a worshipper cannot intend a prayer different from what he is actually performing. A supposed exception for Jumu'ah latecomers, attributed to Imam Muhammad, is analyzed. The lesson clarifies that the established madhhab (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) maintains the rule without exception.

Guided Path
1
1. Recall the general rule
Intention must match the actual prayer being performed. This is a fundamental principle in Hanafi fiqh.
2
2. Identify the alleged exception
Imam Muhammad reportedly allowed a latecomer to Jumu'ah to intend Jumu'ah but pray Zuhr if he caught the imam in tashahhud or sujood al-sahw.
3
3. Evaluate the evidence for the exception
Imam Muhammad’s reasoning: the latecomer did not complete the required rak'ahs for Jumu'ah, so his prayer is actually Zuhr, but he intends Jumu'ah for the reward of congregation.
4
4. Determine the relied-upon position
The madhhab (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) holds that the latecomer prays Jumu'ah, following the imam's prayer. No exception exists.
5
5. Apply the rule in fatwa
The mufta bihi is that intending contrary to actual performance is invalid. A latecomer to Jumu'ah should intend Jumu'ah and complete it as Jumu'ah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مُسْتَلَة : لَيْسَ لِسَاوِ أَنْ يُنْوِى خِلَافَ مَا يُؤَدِى إِلَّا عَلَى قَوْلِ مُحَمَّدٍ فِي الْجُمُعَةِ، فَإِنَّهُ إِذَا أدْرَكَ الْإِمَامَ فِى التَّشَهُدِ، أَوْ فِى سُجُودِ السُّهْوِ نَوَاهَا جُمُعَةٌ، وَيُصَلَّيْهَا ظُهْراً عِنْدَهُ، وَالْمَذْهَبُ أنَّهُ يُصَلِّيْهَا جُمُعَةٌ فَلَا إِسْتِثْنَاءَ. ترجمہ: مثلا کسی نیت کرنے والے کیلئے اس کے خلاف کی نیت کرنا درست نہیں جسے وہ ادا کر رہا ہے مگر ام محمد کے قول پر جمعہ میں، کیونکہ جب امام کو تشہد یا سجدہ سہو میں پائے تو ان کے نزدیک (حکم یہ ہے ) کہ نیت کرے جمعہ کی اور نماز پڑھے ظہر کی اور مذہب یہ ہے کہ جمعہ ہی کی نماز پڑھے، اس لئے اس میں کوئی استثناء نہیں۔ تشریح یہاں مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ موڈی کے خلاف نیت معتبر ہوسکتی ہے یا نہیں؟ تو شیخین کے نزدیک مودی کے خلاف نیت معتبر نہیں ہے علامہ ابن نجیم کی تحقیق کے مطابق امام محمد کے نزدیک ایک مسئلہ میں مودی کے خلاف نیت کا اعتبار ہے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ جب کسی جمعہ میں امام کو تشہد کی حالت میں پایا یا سجدہ سہو کی حالت میں اور وہ شریک ہو گیا تو
Issue: It is not for anyone to intend contrary to what he is performing except according to the statement of Muhammad regarding Jumu'ah. Because if he catches the imam in the tashahhud or in the prostration of forgetfulness, he intends it (the prayer) as Jumu'ah and prays it as Zuhr according to him. And the madhhab is that he prays it as Jumu'ah, so there is no exception. Translation: For example, it is not correct for a person to intend contrary to what he is performing except on the saying of Muhammad in Jumu'ah. Because when he finds the imam in tashahhud or sujood al-sahw, then according to him, he intends it as Jumu'ah and prays it as Zuhr. And the madhhab is that he prays it as Jumu'ah, so there is no exception. Commentary: The issue here is whether an intention contrary to what the mu'addi (the imam) is doing can be valid. According to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), the intention contrary to the mu'addi is not valid. According to the research of Allamah Ibn Nujaym, there is one exception according to Imam Muhammad: when a person joins the Jumu'ah prayer late, catching the imam in tashahhud or sujood al-sahw, then according to Muhammad, he intends Jumu'ah (since he is joining the congregation) but he actually prays Zuhr (because he missed the required number of rak'ahs for Jumu'ah? Actually the text says he intends Jumu'ah but prays it as Zuhr). However, the relied-upon madhhab (the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is that he prays it as Jumu'ah, so there is no exception.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage discusses a fundamental rule of niyyah: a person cannot intend something different from what he is actualy performing (i.e., his intention must match the actual prayer). The only alleged exception, according to Imam Muhammad, is in Jumu'ah prayer for a latecomer who catches the imam in the final sitting (tashahhud) or in the prostration of forgetfulness (sujood al-sahw). According to Muhammad, such a person should intend Jumu'ah (since he is joining the Jumu'ah congregation) but then complete his prayer as Zuhr because he missed the full Jumu'ah. However, the passage clarifies that the established madhhab (of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is that he prays it as Jumu'ah, so there is no real exception. Thus, the rule stands: intending contrary to the actual performance is not permitted.

Key Terms
ساو (sā'ī): A person who intends (from the root 'to intend').
خلاف ما يؤدي (khilāf mā yu'addī): Intending something different from what the imam is actually performing.
الجمعة (al-jumu'ah): The Friday congregational prayer, which has specific rules for latecomers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi madhhab, if a latecomer to Jumu'ah prayer catches the imam in the final tashahhud, what should he intend?
A) He should intend Jumu'ah but complete his prayer as Zuhr.
B) He should intend Zuhr because he missed the main part of Jumu'ah.
C) He should intend Jumu'ah and pray it as Jumu'ah.
D) He should intend the prayer that the imam is performing, which is Jumu'ah, and complete it as Jumu'ah.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule is clear: you cannot intend a prayer different from what you are performing; the alleged exception for Jumu'ah latecomers is not relied upon.

Requirement of Intention of Obligatoriness (Niyyat al-Fardiyyah)
Legal rule with applications on intention of obligatoriness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida 'niyyat al-fardiyyah is only required where confusion with nafl exists' to identify which acts require such intention and which do not.

Core Idea
Intention of fardiyyah is only needed when an act could be fard or nafl and is not inherently distinct.

This lesson explores a key principle in Hanafi ibadat: when must a worshipper specifically intend that an act is obligatory? The answer depends on whether the act could be confused with a supererogatory one. Through applications in hajj, fasting, purification, and prayer, the author demonstrates the scope of this qawida, providing a crucial tool for muftis to determine intention requirements in worship.

Guided Path
1
State the qawida and its condition
Write or recite the maxim: 'لَا تُشْتَرَطُ نِيَّةُ الْفَرْضِيَّةِ إِلَّا فِي مَا يَحْتَمِلُ الْفَرْضَ وَالنَّفْلَ' (Intention of obligatoriness is only required in what could be either obligatory or supererogatory). Note the condition: the act must be ambiguous between fard and nafl.
The condition excludes acts that are inherently distinct (like Ramadan fasts) or purely means (like wudu).
2
Identify acts requiring intention of fardiyyah
From the passage, list the acts that require niyyat al-fardiyyah: hajj performed with absolute intention when fard is due, fasting of kaffarah, and qada fasts of Ramadan. For these, specification is needed because the time also permits nafl performance.
In hajj, Ibn Humam derived that if the person merely intended 'hajj' without specifying fard, the obligation is not fulfilled.
3
Identify acts not requiring intention of fardiyyah
List the acts where niyyat al-fardiyyah is not required: Ramadan fasts (inherently distinct), nafl fasts (intention can be made during the day), wudu and ghusl (no intention required at all), tayammum (only intention of removing hadath suffices), all conditions (shurut) of prayer, the Jumu'ah khutbah, funeral prayer (only fard kifayah), child's prayer, and fard al-ayn vs. fard al-kifayah (apparent view: no requirement).
The rationale for wudu/ghusl: only attainment (husul) is required, not acquisition (tahsil).
4
Understand the underlying rationale
The qawida is based on the principle that intention of fardiyyah is only needed when confusion with nafl is possible. If the act is uniquely fard (like Ramadan fasts) or purely a means (like wudu), specification is unnecessary. The hardship of an act is taken as evidence that it is fard (as in hajj), but the apparent intention governs.
The Hanafi method uses istihsan to turn absolute intention toward obligation when the act involves great difficulty.
5
Apply the qawida to new scenarios
Given a new act of worship, ask: (1) Is the act potentially either fard or nafl? (2) Is there an inherent distinction? (3) Does the act belong to the category of means (wasail) or ends (maqasid)? Apply the qawida to determine if niyyat al-fardiyyah is required.
This analytical process is essential for muftis when addressing contemporary questions about intention in worship.

Translation: And anyway, we have already stated that it (the absolute intention) suffices, but the jurists have explained that it requires that in which matter he intended obligation. The jurists say that he can bear so many difficulties only for the sake of obligation. Hence, Muhaqqiq Ibn Humam extracted that if his reality is that he did not intend obligation, it is not valid, because this absolute intention is turned towards obligation, carrying it upon obligation, acting upon the apparent, and this is excellent. Therefore, in this (hajj) intention of obligation is necessary, because if he intended nafl while hajj was obligatory upon him, his hajj would be nafl. 'We have presented that he performs hajj with absolute intention' – in this 'presented' refers to performing with absolute intention, looking at the standard. The pronoun in 'haml' refers to absolute intention, and in 'alayh' refers to the obligation. Although hajj is valid with absolute intention, in itself intention of obligation is a condition, because the cause of validity with absolute intention is that the jurists mentioned that such great hardships and difficulties are only borne for performing an obligation. As if the jurists have placed the apparent in the rank of the intention found in reality, as will be clarified in the next issue. 'If he launches the intention of hajj by entering ihram for hajj without specifying obligation or nafl, his ihram is valid for hajj and is turned to obligation by istihsan according to the school.' (Raqiya Jadid p. 80) Above it was mentioned that in itself intention is a condition in hajj, but the jurists have placed the apparent in its stead. Therefore, Allamah Ibn Humam derived that if hajj was obligatory upon someone and he performed hajj but his intention was merely to perform hajj, then in the total his intention is considered and the obligatory hajj is not fulfilled. 'And if he intended for another, or for a vow, or for nafl, then it is what he intended, even if he did not perform hajj for obligation.' (Quniya Jadid p. 40) And intention of obligation is necessary in expiations. Therefore, they said that the fast of expiation and making up Ramadan need intention from the night because the time is suitable for nafl fast. Translation: And in expiations intention of obligation is necessary; for this reason the jurists say that in the fast of expiation and making up Ramadan, intention from the night is required because the time also holds the possibility of nafl fast. Elucidation: In the fasts of qada and kaffarah, intention from the night is necessary so that distinction can be made between them and other fasts. But in Ramadan fasts it is not a condition because they are specified by Allah, hence they are distinguished from it, and in nafl it is not a condition because it is established from the Shari' that nafl fast can be kept without prior intention. And qada, absolute vow, and expiations are not valid except with specific intention from the night. (Al-Durr al-Muntaqa with Majma‘ al-Anhur vol. 1, p. 307) As for wudu and ghusl, they have no entry in this discussion due to the absence of requirement of intention in them. As for tayammum, intention of obligation is not required because it is among the means, and we have already stated that intention of removing ritual impurity is sufficient. Translation: And in any case, wudu and ghusl have no connection to this discussion because intention is not required in them. And as for tayammum, intention of obligation is not necessary because it is among the means, and we have already explained that intention of removing ritual impurity is sufficient. Elucidation: Wudu and ghusl have nothing to do with intention of specification, because their attainment is necessary, not their acquisition. Therefore, intention is not required for wudu and ghusl. 'Because what is commanded is nothing but washing and wiping; perhaps this expression indicates that intention is not required for the commanded wudu. Al-Hamawi said: The verification is that the commanded wudu is performed without intention because what is commanded is its attainment, not its acquisition.' (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi Qadim p. 41) In tayammum as well, intention of obligation is not required because tayammum is among the means; therefore intention of removing ritual impurity is sufficient. 'And as for tayammum, intention of obligation is not required because it is among the means, and we have already stated that intention of removing ritual impurity is sufficient.' (Maraqi al-Falah with Sharh Nur al-Idah p. 61 (old)) And upon this, all conditions: intention of obligation is not required for them because of their saying: only their attainment is considered, not their acquisition. Similarly, the khutbah: intention of obligation is not required for it, even if we require intention for it, because it is not performed as nafl. Therefore, the funeral prayer should be similar, because it is only obligatory, as they explicitly stated, and therefore it is not repeated as nafl. And I have not seen the ruling of the child's prayer regarding intention of obligation. It should not be required because it is not obligatory in his case. But he should intend the prayer that Allah has prescribed for the responsible person in this time. And I have not seen either the ruling of intending fard al-ayn in fard al-ayn, and fard al-kifayah in it; the apparent is that it is not required.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul al-iftah work discusses the requirement of intending the obligatoriness (niyyat al-fardiyyah) in acts of worship. The passage type is a legal rule with applications. The author begins by revisiting the earlier principle that an absolute intention (mutilaq niyyah) suffices for hajj, but Ibn Humam derived that if the person actually intended only to perform hajj without distinguishing between fard and nafl, the hajj does not count as the obligatory one. The jurists justify this by the fact that one only bears hardships for obligation. Therefore, in acts that can be either fard or nafl, intention of fardiyyah is required. The passage then applies this to fasting: for kaffarah and qada, intention must be made at night to distinguish from nafl; for Ramadan fasts, it is not needed because they are specified by Allah; for nafl, intention can be made during the day because it is established from practice. Next, acts like wudu and ghusl are excluded from this discussion because intention is not required at all; they are pure means (wasail) whose attainment is required, not the act itself. Similarly, tayammum does not require intention of fardiyyah because it is a means; intention of removing ritual impurity suffices. The passage extends the rule to all conditions (shurut) of worship: they do not require intention of fardiyyah because only their attainment matters, not their acquisition. The khutbah of Jumu'ah, being exclusively fard, also does not require such intention, though intention is required for the prayer itself. The funeral prayer is likewise fard kifayah only, so intention of fardiyyah is not needed. The author then addresses unresolved issues: the prayer of a child (not fard for him) and the distinction between fard al-ayn and fard al-kifayah; in these cases, the apparent view is that intention of fardiyyah is not required. The commentary follows the author's order, explaining each application and the underlying rationale that intention of fardiyyah is only needed when the act could be confused with a supererogatory one.

Key Terms
نِيَّة الْفَرْضِيَّة (niyyat al-fardiyyah): Intention that the act being performed is specifically obligatory, distinguishing it from supererogatory.
مطلق نیت (mutlaq niyyah): Absolute intention of the act without specifying its type (fard/nafl).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, for which of the following acts is intention of fardiyyah required?
A) Wudu
B) Fasting of kaffarah
C) Tayammum
D) Funeral prayer

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school only requires niyyat al-fardiyyah in acts that could be confused with supererogatory ones; otherwise, absolute intention or mere performance suffices.

Intention for Fard Prayers: Specification of Fardiyyah Not Required
Ruling on intention for fard 'ayn and fard kifayah from Fath al-Qadir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the necessity of specifying fardiyyah in intention for fard prayers and identify the exception.

Core Idea
Intending 'Zuhr' is enough; you need not say 'fard' in your heart.

A common question in fiqh is what exactly must be intended when beginning a prayer. This lesson examines a key rule from Fath al-Qadir: for obligatory prayers (fard 'ayn and fard kifayah), the Hanafi school holds that one does not need to specifically intend that the prayer is obligatory. Simply intending the specific prayer, like Zuhr, suffices. There is one exception: the funeral prayer (janazah) requires specification. Understanding this principle helps Muftis advise on valid intention and avoid unnecessary rigidity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
Recognize that the passage is about the intention (niyyah) for fard 'ayn and fard kifayah prayers. The ruling: ta'yin (specification) of fardiyyah is not a condition for validity.
Ta'yin here means specifying that the act is obligatory, not specifying which prayer (e.g., Zuhr).
2
Distinguish Fard 'Ayn and Fard Kifayah
Fard 'ayn are individual obligations like the five daily prayers. Fard kifayah are communal obligations like janazah prayer. The rule applies to both, except janazah.
The exception for janazah is mentioned because its intention requires specifying it is janazah, not merely a prayer.
3
Understand the Sufficiency of Specifying the Prayer
The passage states it is enough to intend 'Zuhr' etc. Without adding 'fard'. This is the mufta bihi position.
The rationale is that the legal category (fardiyyah) is inherent in the act; intending the specific act automatically includes its obligation.
4
Apply the Rule in Fatwa Context
When a mustafti asks about the validity of a prayer where one did not explicitly intend 'fard', the Mufti can rule it valid based on this principle.
This ruling is part of Rasm al-Mufti: rely on the clear hadith and ease.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نے فتح القدیر میں اس کا حکم دیکھا ہے کہ فرض عین میں بلا کسی اختلاف کے نیت شرط نہیں ہے اور اسی طرح فرض کفایہ خلا جنازہ کی نماز میں بھی اس کی تعیین شرم نہیں ہے۔ (قوله) ولم ار حكم نية فرض العين الخ على ما علت لا يلزم تعيين الفرضية بل يكفيه نية الظهر مثلا فلا يلزم ايضاً نية فرض العين او الكفاية بعد ما عينه بما ذكر ( تقريرات الرافعي ص:۵۰)
He saw in Fath al-Qadir the ruling that for fard 'ayn, without any disagreement, intention (of fardiyyah) is not a condition, and similarly for fard kifayah, except for the funeral prayer, its specification is not a condition. (His saying) I did not see the ruling of intention of fard 'ayn, etc. According to what is established, specification of the fardiyyah is not necessary, rather it suffices for him to intend 'Zuhr' for example, so also specification of fard 'ayn or kifayah is not necessary after he has specified it with what was mentioned. (Taqrirat al-Rafi'i p.50)
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from Fath al-Qadir regarding the intention in obligatory prayers. The key point is that for fard 'ayn (individual obligations like the five daily prayers), one does not need to specifically intend that the prayer is fard. It is enough to intend the specific prayer, e.g., 'I am praying Zuhr'. The same applies to fard kifayah (communal obligations) except for the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) where specification is required. The passage then quotes the original matn: 'I did not see a ruling on intention of fard 'ayn...' This emphasizes that the shar'i requirement is not to intend the legal category (fardiyyah) but to specify the act itself. This is a distinct Hanafi position, as some other schools require intention of fardiyyah for valid worship. The passage clarifies that as long as one specifies the prayer (e.g., Zuhr), that suffices; one need not add 'as fard' in the intention.

Key Terms
فرض عین (fard 'ayn): Individual obligation: every Muslim must perform it personally, e.g., five daily prayers.
تعیین (ta'yin): Specification: here it means specifying whether the prayer is fard or not in the intention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passed passage, which of the following is sufficient for the intention of a fard 'ayn prayer?
A) Intending the prayer as fard
B) Intending the specific prayer (e.g., Zuhr)
C) Both A and B
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
For most obligatory prayers, intending the specific prayer is enough; specifying fardiyyah is not required, except for janazah prayer.
