Intention in I'ada Prayer Due to Makruh or Wajib Omission
Ruling on intention in i'ada prayer based on scholarly disagreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim regarding the nature of i'ada prayer and state the correct intention when repeating a prayer due to makruh or omission of wajib.

Core Idea
When repeating a prayer due to a flaw, the second prayer is compensatory (jabirah), not a new fard, so intention should be for compensation.

When a prayer is repeated because it involved a makruh tahrimi or omitted a wajib, scholars differ on the nature of the second prayer. The predominant Hanafi view holds that the second prayer is compensatory (jabirah) and essentially nafl, so the intention should be for compensation, not fard. This lesson unpacks the rule and its practical application for a mufti.

Guided Path
1
Identify key terms
Start by understanding the terms 'i'ada' (repetition) and 'jabirah' (compensatory). Recognize that the passage discusses the nature of the repeated prayer.
The term 'jabirah' indicates that the prayer makes up for a deficiency without being the original fard.
2
Distinguish the two scholarly positions
Identify the two views: (1) The repeated prayer is jabirah (nafl) and intends compensation. (2) The repeated prayer is the actual fard and requires intention of fardiyyah.
The first view is attributed to Haskafi and Ibn Nujaym; the second is mentioned as an alternative view.
3
Determine the mufta bihi position
Analyze the author's conclusion: the first view is the relied-upon position for fatwa. The second view is less preferred.
This is a rasm al-mufti rule: the mufti should follow the majority view unless there is strong evidence otherwise.
4
Apply to a concrete scenario
Suppose a person performed Zuhr prayer but inadvertently omitted a wajib (e.g., missed a sajda). He repeats the prayer. According to the mufta bihi, he should intend 'I repeat this prayer to compensate for the deficiency in my fard.'
He does not intend it as a new fard, because the original fard obligation is already discharged.
5
Note the subsidiary ruling (fa'ida)
The passage adds that i'ada is wajib if due to omitting a wajib, sunnah if due to omitting a sunnah, and mustahabb if due to a makruh tanzihi. This helps determine when i'ada is required.
This is important for a mufti to know the gradation of rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا الصَّلَاةُ المُعَادَةُ لإِرْتِكَابِ مَكْرُوْهِ، أَوَ تَرْكِ وَاجِبٍ: فَلَاشَكُ أَنَّهَا جَابِرَةٌ، لَا فَرْضٌ لِقَوْلِهِمْ بِسُقُوْطِ الْفَرْضِ بِالأوْلى فَعَلَى هَذَا يَنْوِي كَوْنَهَا جَائِزَةٌ لِنَقْضِ الْقَرْضِ عَلَىٰ أَنَّهَا نقل تحقيقاً وَأمَّا عَلَى الْقَوْلِ : بأن القَرْضَ يَسْقُطُ بِهَا، فَلَاحِفَاءَ فِي اشْتِرَاطِ نِيَّةِ الْفَرْضِيَّةِ. ترجمہ: اور بہر حال وہ نماز جو لوٹائی جائے کسی مکروہ کے ارتکاب یا ترک واجب کی وجہ سے تو کوئی شک نہیں کہ نقص کو پوری کرنے والی ہے فرض نہیں ہے فقہاء کے کہنے کی وجہ سے کہ فرض پہلی سے ساقط ہو جاتا ہے تو اس کے لئے نیت کرے گا کہ وہ فرض کی کمی کو پورا کرنے والی ہے اس بناء پر کہ وہ حقیقت میں نفل ہے اور بہر حال اس قول پر کہ اس کے ذریعہ فرض ساقط ہوتا ہے، تو خفا نہیں فرضیت کی نیت کے شرط ہونے میں۔ تشریح اگر کوئی نماز مکروہ تحریمی کے ارتکاب یا ترک واجب کی وجہ سے لوٹائی جارہی ہے تو دوسری نماز میں کیا نیت ہونی چاہئے تو اس کا دارو مدار اس بات پر ہے کہ دوسری نماز کی حیثیت کیا ہے ایک فریق کی رائے یہ ہے کہ پہلی نماز فرض تھی جس سے فرض ساقط ہو گیا البتہ اس میں کچھ کمی واقع ہو گئی تھی اس کمی اور نقص کو پورا کرنے کے لئے نماز کا اعادہ کیا جارہا ہے لہذا اس میں یہ نیت کی جائے گی کہ میں فرض میں نقصان کی تلافی کے لئے نماز پڑھ رہا ہوں اس لئے کہ فرض تو نماز اول سے ساقط ہو گیا اور یہ دوسری نماز اصل میں نفل ہے جس کا مقصد نقصان فرض کی تلافی ہے جیسا کہ علامہ حصکفی اور ابن نجیم نے تصریح کی ہے۔ دوسرے فریق کی رائے یہ ہے کہ دوسری نماز ہی اصل نماز ہے اس قول کی بنیاد پر دوسری نماز میں فرضیت کی نیت ضروری ہوگی چونکہ اول نماز میں خلل پیدا ہو گیا جس کی وجہ سے وہ اصل نماز نہ رہی۔ علامہ شامی کی رائے یہ ہے کہ دونوں نمازوں کی حیثیت فرض کی ہے لیکن پہلی نماز فرض ناقص ہے اور دوسری نماز فرضِ کامل ہے۔ (کم ہونہ کورفی شامی زکریا ۲ ج:۵۲۲) فائده: الاعادة ان كانت لترك واجب فواجبة وان كانت لترك سنة فسنة وان كانت لارتكاب مكروه تنزيهى فمستحب.
As for the prayer repeated for committing a disliked act or omitting an obligatory act: there is no doubt that it is compensatory, not the fard, because of their saying that the fard is dropped by the first. So on this, he intends it to be compensatory for the deficiency of the fard, while in reality it is nafl. And according to the opinion that the fard is dropped by it (the second), there is no concealment regarding the condition of intending the fardiyyah. Translation: As for the prayer repeated for committing a disliked act or omitting an obligatory act, there is no doubt that it is compensatory, not the fard, because of the scholars' saying that the fard is dropped by the first. So he will intend it to compensate for the deficiency of the fard, on the basis that it is actually nafl. And according to the saying that the fard is dropped by this (second prayer), there is no concealment that intending fardiyyah is a condition. Explanation: ... Benefit: The repetition is obligatory if due to omitting a wajib, sunnah if due to omitting a sunnah, and mustahabb if due to committing a makruh tanzihi.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage discusses the intention in a repeated prayer (i'ada) when the original prayer involved a makruh tahrimal or omission of a wajib. The core issue is the nature of the second prayer. There are two views: (1) The second prayer is compensatory (jabirah) and essentially nafl, so one intends it as compensation, not as fard. This is the view of Haskafi and Ibn Nujaym. (2) The second prayer is the actual fard, so one must intend fardiyyah. 'Allama Shami reconciles by saying both are fard but the first is deficient and the second is complete. The passage then gives a fa'ida about the ruling of i'ada: it is wajib if due to leaving a wajib, sunnah if due to leaving a sunnah, mustahabb if due to a makruh tanzihi.

Key Terms
اعادہ (i'ada): The act of repeating a prayer due to a flaw in the original
جابره (jabirah): Compensatory prayer that makes up for deficiency but is not itself the fard

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority view in this passage, what should one intend in the i'ada prayer?
A) Fard of that time
B) Compensation for the deficiency of the fard
C) Nafl without specification
D) The specific prayer as qada

Key Takeaway
When repeating a prayer due to a makruh or omission of a wajib, the second prayer is compensatory (jabirah), not a new fard, and the intention should be for compensation.

Validity of Worship with Mistaken Intention of Ada/Qada
This passage states a Hanafi rasm al-mufti principle and provides illustrative scenarios.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim that error in specifying ada versus qada is excused when the original intention (asl al-niyya) is present, and distinguish valid from invalid intentions in worship.

Core Idea
A mistake between ada and qada does not invalidate worship if the heart intended the underlying obligation.

This lesson introduces a critical principle for muftis: in acts of worship, an honest error in distinguishing between ada (timely performance) and qada (make-up) does not invalidate the act as long as the worshipper intended the fundamental obligation. The source passage from Kashf al-Asrar clarifies that the presence of 'asl al-niyya' (the core intention for the specific worship) is sufficient. Understanding this rule prevents unnecessary invalidation and provides flexibility in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the Maxim
Read the central maxim: 'Ada is valid with the intention of qada, and qada with the intention of ada, as long as the original intention is present.' This is the foundation.
The maxim is a dabt (restrictive sub-maxim) under the larger qawida 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha'.
2
Identify the Key Condition
The condition is 'asl al-niyya' — the intention for the specific obligatory act (e.g., intention to pray Zuhr or fast Ramadan). The distinction between ada and qada is not a condition.
The legal definition dissector breaks down 'asl al-niyya' into its components.
3
Study the Examples
Review the four furuat from the text: (1) Zuhr prayed after time thinking time remains, (2) captive fasting after Ramadan intending ada, (3) Zuhr prayed before time thinking time passed, (4) captive fasting in Ramadan intending qada. In all cases, the worship is valid because the core intention matches the obligation.
Notice that the actual time does not affect validity; the intention governs.
4
Recognize the Exception
The maxim applies only when the original intention of the fard of the time is present. If a person intends a completely different prayer (e.g., intending Asr when it is Zuhr), the worship is invalid because the core intention is absent.
This is the istithna' (exception) governed by 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha'.
5
Apply the Principle to New Cases
As a mufti, you will encounter scenarios where a worshipper mistakenly thought the time was different. Use the maxim to determine validity: check if the person intended the correct fard of that moment. If yes, the error in temporal specification is excused.
This principle also applies to Hajj, where specification is not required at all.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَ اخْتَلَفُوْا أَنَّ الْوَقْتِيَّةَ هَلْ تَجُوْزُ بِنِيَّةِ الْقَضَاءِ؟ وَ الْمُخْتَارُ الْجَوَازُ إِذَا كَانَ فِي قَلْبِهِ فَرْضُ الْوَقْتِ وَكَذَا الْقَضَاءُ بِنِيَّةِ الْآدَاءِ هُوَ الْمُخْتَارُ. ترجمہ: اور فقہاء کا اس میں اختلاف ہے کہ وقتیہ نماز قضاء کی نیت سے جائز ہے؟ پسندیدہ قول جواز کا ہے اس لئے کہ اس کے دل میں فرض الوقت ہے اور ایسے ہی قضاء ادا کی نیت سے یہی مختار ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ وقتیہ نماز قضاء کی نیت سے درست ہو سکتی ہے یا نہیں؟ تو اس سلسلہ میں قول مختار یہ ہے کہ جب مصلی کے دل میں وقت کے فرض کی نیت ہو تو درست ہو سکتی ہے اسی طرح قضا بھی ادا کی نیت سے درست ہوسکتی ہے۔ وَذُكِرَ فِي كَشْفِ الأَسْرَارِ شَرْحِ أُصُولِ فَخرِ الْإِسْلَامِ أَنَّ الْآدَاءَ يَصِحُ بِنِيَّةِ الْقَضَاءِ حَقِيْقَةٌ كَنِيَّةٍ مَنْ نَوَى أَدَاءَ ظُهْرِ الْيَوْمِ بَعْدَ حُرُوْجِ الْوَقْتِ عَلَى ظَنِّ أَنَّ الْوَقْتَ بَاقِ، وَكَنِيَّةِ الأَسِيرِ الَّذِي إِشْتَبَه عَلَيْهِ شَهْرُ رَمَضَانَ، فَتَحَوَّى شَهْراً، وَصَامَهُ بِنِيَّةِ الْآدَاءِ، فَوَقَعَ صَوْمُهُ بَعْدَ رَمَضَانَ وَعَكْسُهُ، كَنِيَّةِ مَنْ نَوَى قَضَاءَ الظُّهْرِ عَلَى ظَنِّ أَنَّ الْوَقْتَ قَدْ خَرَجَ، وَلَمْ يَخْرُجْ بَعْدُ وَكَنِيَّةِ الْأَسِيْرِ الَّذِى صَامَ رَمَضَانَ بِنِيَّةِ الْقَضَاءِ عَلَى ظَنِّ أَنَّهُ قَدْ مَضَى وَالصَّحَّةُ فِيهِ بِااعْتِبَارِ أَنَّهُ أَتَى بِأصْلِ النِّيَّةِ، وَلَكِنَّهُ أَخْطَأ فِى الظَّنِّ وَالْخَطَأُ فِي مِثْلِهِ مَعْفُو، إنتهى، وَأَمَّا الْحَج فَيَنبَغِى أن لا تُشْتَرَطَ فِيهِ بيَّة التمييز بَيْنَ الْآدَاءِ وَالْقَضَاءِ :ترجمہ: اور کشف الاسرار شرح اصول فخر الاسلام میں مذکور ہے کہ دا قضاء کی نیت سے حقیقی مسیح ہوجاتی ہے جیسے اس شخص کی نیت جس نے وقت کے نکل جانے کے بعد آج کے ظہر کی اداء کی نسبت کی یہ خیال کرتے ہوئے کہ وقت باقی ہے، اور جیسے اس قیدی کی نیت جس پر رمضان کا مہینہ مشتبہ ہو جائے ، اور اس نے مہینہ میں غور فکر کیا اوراد کی نیت سے روزہ رکھا اور اس کا روزہ رمضان کے بعد ہوا اور اس کے برعکس جیسے اس کی نیت جس نے نظر کی نام کا نیت کی یہ گمان کرتے ہوئے کہ وقت نکل چکا حالانکہ وقت ابھی تک نہیں نکلا ۔ اور جیسے اس قیدی کی نیت جس نے رمضان کا روزہ رکھا قضاء کی نیت سے یہ گمان کرتے ہوئے کہ رمضان گذر چکا اور صحت اس میں اس اعتبار سے ہے کہ اصل نیت کے ساتھ ادا کیا لیکن گمان میں چوک کی اور اس جیسے میں چوک معاف ہے، کشف الاسرار شرح اصول فخر الاسلام کا کلام پورا ہوا۔ تشریح: اوانیت قضاء اور قضاء بنیت ادا سے متعلق چند جزئیات ذکر کی جارہی ہیں، فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر حقی ہی قضاء کی نیت ہو تو بھی ادا درست ہو جاتی ہے، جیسے اگر کوئی شخص آج کے ظہر کی نماز ادا پڑھارہا ہے وقت نکل جانے کے اور بہر حال حج تو مناسب یہ ہے کہ اس میں ادا اور قضاء کے مابین تمیز کی نیت شرط نہ ہو۔ بت کی تو اس مثال میں قضاء بہ نیت اور پائی گئی۔ بعد اور گمان یہ ہے کہ ابھی وقت باقی ہے تو اس کی یہ نماز قضا ہوئی اور اس نے یہ مجھ کر پڑھی ہے کہ وقت باقی ہے تو ادا کی وكنية الاسير : کوئی شخص قید میں تھا اور وہ دنیا کے حالات سے بالکل بے خبر تھا اس نے محض تحری اور اندازہ کر کے روزے رکھے اس نے یہ روزے ادا کی نیت سے رکھے تھے لیکن اس کے یہ روزے رمضان کے مہینہ کے بعد رکھے گئے یا بعض رمضان کے مہینہ میں اور بعض بعد میں تو اس کے روزے بیچ ہو جائیں گے کیونکہ اس نے ادا کی نیت سے پاروزے رکھے ہیں ۔ و عكسه كنية من نوى : اگر کسی نے ادا نماز قضاء کی نیت سے پڑھی یہ سمجھ کر کہ وقت نکل چکا ہے حالانکہ باقی خان اس کی نماز درست ہو جائے گی اور سیادا نیت قضاء کی مثال ہے۔ وكنية الاسير الذی صام رمضان کسی قیدی نے علم نہ ہونے پر رمضان کے مہینہ میں قضاء کی نیت سے روزے رکھے تو اس کے یہ روزے رمضان کے اداروزوں میں شمار ہوں گے، کیونکہ اصل نیت پائی گئی لیکن گمان کی وجہ سے اس سے خطا ہو گئی اور اس جیسی خطا معاف ہے۔ والصحة فيه: مذکورہ جزئیات میں اصل عبادت اور تعیین فرضیت کی نیت پائی گئی جوضروری ہے اور اداو قضا کی نیت ضروری نہیں ہے، اور جو چوک ہوئی ہے اس میں ہوئی ہے جو غیر لازم تھی اس لئے وہ چوک مصنر نہیں ہے۔ راما الحج حج میں ادا اور قضاء کی تعیین ضروری نہیں ، کوئی شخص حج کی نیت کرے تو نیت میں اداء حج یا قضاء ج کی مین شرط نہیں ہے لہذا ا دا اور قضاء میں تمیز کرنے کے لئے نیت شرط نہیں ہے۔
And they differed: Is the time-bound (prayer) permissible with the intention of qada? The chosen view is permissibility, because the obligation of the time is in his heart. Likewise, qada with the intention of ada is the chosen view. In Kashf al-Asrar, Sharh Usul Fakhr al-Islam, it is mentioned that ada becomes valid with the intention of qada, truly, like the intention of one who intended to perform the Zuhr of today after the time had left, thinking that the time remained; and like the intention of a captive for whom the month of Ramadan became ambiguous, so he estimated a month and fasted it with the intention of ada, and his fast fell after Ramadan. And its opposite: like the intention of one who intended to make up Zuhr thinking that the time had passed, but it had not yet passed; and like the intention of the captive who fasted Ramadan with the intention of qada, thinking that it had passed. And correctness in it is because he performed the original intention, but he erred in the assumption, and error in such matters is excused. As for Hajj, it is befitting that the intention to distinguish between ada and qada is not required for it.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the effect of mistaken specification in the intention of worship. The text begins by citing a difference of opinion: whether a time-bound prayer performed with the intention of qada (make-up) is valid. The chosen (muhtar) position is that it is valid because the essential intention of the time's obligation is present. Similarly, performing a make-up prayer with the intention of ada (current time) is also valid. The commentator then quotes Kashf al-Asrar: the correctness is based on the fact that the original intention (asl al-niyya) was present; the error in the specific designation (ada vs. qada) is excused. The examples clarify: a person prays Zuhr after the time, thinking the time remains; the prayer is valid as ada because his heart intended the current obligation. A captive fasts during Ramadan thinking it is past; his fast counts as Ramadan. In all cases, the key is the presence of the intention for the fundamental obligation (the fard of the time or the fard of Ramadan). As for Hajj, there is no requirement to specify ada or qada; any valid intention for Hajj suffices. This ruling is a rasm al-mufti principle: in worship, the specification of ada or qada is not a condition for validity when the underlying obligation is correctly intended.

Key Terms
أَصْلُ النِّيَّةِ (asl al-niyya): The basic intention to perform the obligatory worship (e.g., intention to pray Zuhr or fast Ramadan) without the need to specify ada or qada.
الْآدَاءُ (al-ada): Performing the worship in its appointed time.
الْقَضَاءُ (al-qada): Performing the worship after its appointed time, as a make-up.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the maxim in this lesson, what is the single most important element for the validity of a prayer when a person mistakenly prays Zuhr with the intention of qada after the time has actually left?
A) The prayer must be repeated later with the correct intention.
B) The person's heart must have intended the obligation of Zuhr (fard al-waqt).
C) The prayer is invalid because the intention was qada but the time was past.
D) The person must have explicitly said 'I intend to pray Zuhr as qada'.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, an honest error between ada and qada is excused if the worshipper intended the fundamental obligation; the core intention (asl al-niyya) is what matters.

Slaughtering for Other than Allah: Ruling and Dispute on Takfir
Fatwa ruling on slaughter for ta'zim with internal dispute on takfir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that slaughtering to honor a person (ta'zim) renders the meat carrion, identify the internal dispute on takfir, and apply the distinction between ta'zim and hospitality (diyafah).

Core Idea
Slaughtering to honor a person makes the meat carrion; takfir of the slaughterer is disputed within the Hanafi school.

This passage from al-Bazzaziyya addresses a serious boundary in fiqh: when does an act of slaughter cross from permissible hospitality into prohibited shirk? The ruling on the meat is clear: it becomes carrion. However, the scholars differ on whether the slaughterer himself becomes a disbeliever. Understanding this nuance is essential for any mufti, as the consequences of takfir are far-reaching.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the clear ruling
The act is slaughtering an animal for a person returning from Hajj, war, or an amir with the intention of honoring them. The ruling is that the animal becomes carrion (maytah).
The word 'maytah' means it is haram to eat.
2
Recognize the internal dispute on takfir
Scholars differ on whether the slaughterer becomes a disbeliever. Some (al-Safkardari, al-Nasafi, al-Hakim) say he is declared kafir; others (al-Fadali, Isma'il al-Zahid) say he is not.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Understand the key distinction: ta'zim vs diyafah
The commentary clarifies that the ruling of carrion applies when the intent is to honor the person (ta'zim). If the intent is hospitality (diyafah) or feeding guests, the meat remains halal.
Hospitality is a sunnah and does not negate the dhabh.
4
Apply the distinction to a fatwa scenario
When issuing a fatwa, the mufti must ascertain the intention. If the slaughterer intended ta'zim, the meat is haram; if diyafah, it is halal. The issue of takfir requires additional caution.
The mufti should not rush to declare takfir; seek clarification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَصَرَّحَ فِي الْبَزَّازِيَّةِ مِنْ الْفَاظِ التَّكْفِيرِ أَنَّ الذَّبْحَ لِلْقَادِمِ مِنْ حَجِّ، أَوْ غَزْوِ، أَوْ ار از غيْره يَجْعَل المذبوح ميْنةً. وَاخْتَلَفُوا في كفر الذابح فَالشَّيْخُ السَّفَكَرْدَرى وعبد الوَاحِدِ الدَّرْقِيُّ الحَدِيدِيُّ، وَالنِّسَفِيُّ وَالْحَاكِمُ عَلَى أَنَّهُ يُكَفَّرُ، وَالْفَضَلِيُّ وَ إسْمَاعِيلُ الزَّاهِدُ عَلَى أَنَّهُ لَا يُكَفَّرُ، إِنْتَهَى.
And it is stated explicitly in al-Bazzaziyya, from the words of takfir, that slaughtering for the one arriving from Hajj, or war, or an amir, or other than them, makes the slaughtered animal carrion. And they differed concerning the disbelief of the slaughterer: al-Shaykh al-Safkardari, Abd al-Wahid al-Darqi al-Hadidi, al-Nasafi, and al-Hakim are of the opinion that he is to be declared a disbeliever; while al-Fadali and Isma'il al-Zahid are of the opinion that he is not to be declared a disbeliever. End.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage from al-Bazzaziyya addresses a serious issue: if a person slaughters an animal to honor a returning pilgrim, warrior, or an amir (ruler), the animal becomes carrion (maytah) — i.e., it is not Halal. The act is considered slaughtering for other than Allah (ahlun li-ghayrillah). Scholars differ on whether the slaughterer himself becomes a disbeliever (kafir). A group of scholars including al-Safkardari, al-Darqi, al-Nasafi, and al-Hakim rule that he does become a disbeliever because the act is tantamount to shirk. However, al-Fadali and Isma'il al-Zahid hold that he does not become a disbeliever, perhaps because the intention may not be worship of the person but merely hospitality. The commentary (tashrih) then explains that the ruling applies only when the purpose is to honor the person (ta'zim). If the purpose is feeding guests (diyafah or hospitality), it is not Haram and the meat remains Halal, as it is a form of honoring the guest which is Sunnah of Ibrahim (AS) and is ultimately for Allah's sake.

Key Terms
ذبح لغير الله (dhabh li-ghayrillah): Slaughtering an animal with the intention of honoring someone other than Allah, making the meat carrion.
ميته (maytah): Carrion; an animal not slaughtered Islamically, thus haram to eat.
تكفير (takfir): Declaring a Muslim to be a disbeliever due to an act or statement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on the meat of an animal slaughtered for the arrival of an amir with the intention of honoring him?
A) The meat is halal because the name of Allah was mentioned.
B) The meat is carrion (maytah) and haram.
C) The meat is halal only if the amir is a Muslim.
D) The meat is halal if the slaughterer is not a disbeliever.

Key Takeaway
Slaughtering to honor a person (ta'zim) renders the meat carrion; takfir of the slaughterer is disputed, and the distinction between ta'zim and diyafah is crucial for fatwa.

Slaughter for a Traveler's Arrival and the Takfir Dispute
Ruling on slaughter for traveler and takfir dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the ruling on slaughter for a traveler's arrival in the Hanafi school and evaluate the internal disagreement on takfir of the slaughterer.

Core Idea
Slaughter for the honor of a traveler renders the animal carrion; the takfir of the slaughterer is disputed among Hanafi scholars.

This passage from al-Bazzaziyya and later commentaries addresses a critical issue in personal practice and fatwa: slaughtering an animal to honor a returning traveler. The ruling hinges on intention—if the purpose is honorific dedication, it is akin to dedicating to other than Allah and makes the animal carrion. If it is hospitality, it remains halal. The passage also records a significant ikhtilaf among authoritative Hanafi scholars on whether the slaughterer commits kufr. This lesson unpacks the ruling and the dispute, highlighting the caution required in issuing fatwa on such matters.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the act
Identify the specific act described: slaughter for a person arriving from Hajj, ghazw, or amir. Note that the act is evaluated based on the intention behind it.
The act itself is not inherently forbidden; its ruling depends on the purpose.
2
Identify the ruling on the animal
According to al-Bazzaziyya, if the slaughter is for the honor of the arriving person, the animal becomes carrion (maytah) and is impermissible.
This is because the slaughter is directed to other than Allah (ighlal li ghayr Allah).
3
Understand the role of intention
If the intention is hospitality (not honor), the slaughter is permissible, as it follows the sunnah of Ibrahim and honors Allah.
Intention (niyyah) differentiates between halal and haram in this context.
4
Analyze the takfir dispute
List the scholars on both sides: those who say the slaughterer becomes a kafir (e.g., al-Safakardari, al-Darqi, al-Nasafi, al-Hakim) and those who say he does not (al-Fadali, Ismail al-Zahid). Understand their reasoning.
The dispute is internal to the Hanafi school and remains unresolved in the text.
5
Extract the fatwa implication
The mufta bihi ruling: the animal is carrion when slaughtered for honor. Takfir is not definitively pronounced; caution is required. Avoid such slaughter entirely to prevent sin.
Later sources like Shami confirm the ikhtilaf and advise against the practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَصَرَّحَ فِي الْبَزَّازِيَّةِ مِنْ الْفَاظِ التَّكْفِيرِ أَنَّ الذَّبْحَ لِلْقَادِمِ مِنْ حَجِّ، أَوْ غَزْوِ، أَوْ ار از غيْره يَجْعَل المذبوح ميْنةً. وَاخْتَلَفُوا في كفر الذابح فَالشَّيْخُ السَّفَكَرْدَرى وعبد الوَاحِدِ الدَّرْقِيُّ الحَدِيدِيُّ، وَالنِّسَفِيُّ وَالْحَاكِمُ عَلَى أَنَّهُ يُكَفَّرُ، وَالْفَضَلِيُّ وَ إسْمَاعِيلُ الزَّاهِدُ عَلَى أَنَّهُ لَا يُكَفَّرُ، إِنْتَهَى.
ترجمه اور بزاز یہ میں تصریح ہے تکفیر کے الفاظ کی کہ حج یا غزوہ یا امیر یا اس کے علاوہ آنے والے کے لئے امنا کرنا نہ بوت کو مردار بنادیتا ہے۔ اور ون کرنے والے کے کفر میں علماء کا اختلاف ہے چنانچہ شیخ سفکر دری عبدالواحد درقی حدیدی نسفی اور حاکم یہ کہتے ہیں کہ س کی تکفیر کی جائے گی اور فضلی اور اسماعیل زاہد یہ کہتے ہیں کہ تکفیر نہیں کی جائے گی بزاز یہ کا کلام پورا ہوا۔ تشریح: اگر کسی شخص نے حاجتی یا محامد یا امیر یا ان کے علاوہ کسی کے اعزاز میں جانور ذبح کیا تو بزازیہ کے الفاظ کفیر میں ہے کہ وہ جانور مردار ہو جائے گا یہ اس وقت ہے جبکہ ذبح سے مقصود تعظیم کرنا ہو اور اگر مقصد آنے والوں کی خیالات اور مہمان نوازی کرنا ہو تو حرام نہیں ہوگا اور نہ ہی مردار ہوگا بلکہ وہ بدستور حلال ہوگا اور اس کا کھانا درست ہوگا۔ ذبح لقدوم الأمير ونحوه كواحد من العظماء يحرم لانه اهل لغير الله ولو ذكر اسم الله العالى ولم ذبح للضيف لا يحرم لانه سنة الخليل واكرام الضيف اكراماً لله تعالى (شامی ج ۹ : ۴۳۹)
واختلفوا في كفر الذابح : اگر کسی نے غیر اللہ کے اعزاز میں جانور ذبح کیا تو اس کا ذبح کرنے والا کافر ہوگا یا نہیں؟ اس سلسلہ میں فقہاء کا اختلاف ہے شیخ مفکر دری عبدالواحد در قی حدیدی بسی اور حاکم شہید اس بات کے قائل ہیں کہ کافر ہو جائے گا علامہ فضلی اور اسماعیل زاہدی اس کے قائل ہیں کہ کا فرنہیں ہوگا۔
و ان لم يقدمها لياكل منها بل يدفعها لغيره كان لتعظيم غير الله فتحرم وهل يكفر قولان (شامی ۹، ص: ۴۴۹)
And it is explicitly stated in al-Bazzaziyya, from the expressions of takfir, that slaughter for the arrival of one from Hajj or ghazw or amir or other than that makes the slaughtered animal carrion. And they differed regarding the kufr of the slaughterer: al-Shaykh al-Safakardari, Abd al-Wahid al-Darqi al-Hadidi, al-Nasafi, and al-Hakim opined that he becomes a disbeliever; al-Fadali and Ismail al-Zahid opined that he does not become a disbeliever. End. Translation: And in al-Bazzaziyya it is explicitly mentioned from the words of takfir that slaughtering for a person arriving from Hajj or ghazw or amir or other than that renders the slaughtered animal carrion. And there is disagreement among scholars regarding the kufr of the slaughterer. Accordingly, al-Shaykh al-Safakardari, Abd al-Wahid al-Darqi al-Hadidi, al-Nasafi, and al-Hakim say that takfir should be applied, while al-Fadali and Ismail al-Zahid say that takfir should not be applied. The speech of al-Bazzaziyya is complete. Explanation: If a person slaughters an animal in honor of a hajji or a warrior or an amir or anyone else, then according to the words of al-Bazzaziyya regarding kufr, that animal becomes carrion. This is when the purpose is to honor them. But if the purpose is hospitality and welcoming guests, then it is not forbidden, nor does it become carrion; rather it remains halal and eating it is permissible. 'Slaughter for the arrival of an amir and the like, for a great person, is forbidden because it is dedicating to other than Allah, even if he mentions Allah's name. But slaughter for a guest is not forbidden because it is the sunnah of Ibrahim and honoring a guest is honoring Allah.' (Shami vol. 9, p. 439) And they differed regarding the kufr of the slaughterer: if someone slaughters an animal in honor of other than Allah, does the slaughterer become a disbeliever or not? There is disagreement among the fuqaha: al-Shaykh al-Mufakir [?] al-Darqi al-Hadidi al-Basi and al-Hakim al-Shahid are of the view that he becomes a disbeliever; Allama al-Fadali and Ismail al-Zahidi are of the view that he does not become a disbeliever. And if he does not present it for eating from it but rather gives it to someone else for the purpose of glorifying other than Allah, then it is forbidden and whether he becomes a disbeliever has two opinions. (Shami vol. 9, p. 449)
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage addresses the crucial issue of slaughtering animals for the sake of someone other than Allah. It establishes that if the slaughter is performed to honor a returning traveler (hajj, ghazw, or a dignitary), the animal becomes carrion (maytah) because it is akin to dedicating the slaughter to other than Allah. The purpose matters: if the intent is hospitality and welcoming, it remains halal, as it follows the sunnah of Prophet Ibrahim and is ultimately for Allah's sake. The passage then records a significant ikhtilaf among Hanafi scholars: whether the person who performs such a slaughter commits kufr. This is a grave classification. The names of several scholars are given who hold differing positions: some say takfir, others say not. The authority weight is from later fatwa works (Bazzaziyya, Shami) and not from Zahir al-Riwayah. The practical fatwa (thamar al-khilaf) is that one should avoid such slaughter due to the serious difference and the risk of it being carrion. The ikhtilaf shows the caution of the Hanafi school towards any act that might imply shirk.

Key Terms
الذبح للقادم (al-dhabh li al-qadim): slaughter performed in honor of an arriving person (hajji, warrior, ruler)
تكفير (takfir): declaring someone to be a disbeliever

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view cited, what is the ruling if someone slaughters an animal to honor a returning hajji?
A) It is permissible because the hajji is a pious person.
B) The animal becomes carrion and is forbidden.
C) It is makruh but halal.
D) It is valid only if the slaughterer is a Muslim.

Key Takeaway
Slaughter for the honor of a traveler is forbidden and renders the animal carrion; the takfir of the slaughterer remains an unresolved internal Hanafi dispute requiring caution.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Luqmah, Riya, and Ijarah: Hanafi Rasm Rulings on Intention and Compensation in Worship
Rasm rule with furu' applications and intra-school ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'al-riya la yadkhul al-fara'id' to cases of worldly motives in obligatory acts, and identify the mufta bihi position on ijarah for worship.

Core Idea
Teaching intention breaks prayer; worldly motive does not break obligation; ijarah on worship is now permitted by later Hanafi fatwa.

This passage from the Ashbah wa al-Nazair tradition addresses two distinct but related rasm rulings: the effect of teaching intention during prayer, and the role of worldly compensation in obligatory acts. Both rulings hinge on the Hanafi school's nuanced understanding of intention (niyyah) and contracts. You will learn how a seemingly mundane act like prompting someone in prayer can invalidate it, and why praying for a monetary reward still fulfills the obligation without entitling you to the money.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the first ruling: prompting (luqmah) with teaching intention
Identify the condition: the act of prompting someone other than one's imam with the intention to teach. Determine the ruling: prayer becomes invalid because it resembles ordinary speech. Note the exception: if the intention is merely to recite correctly (tilaawah) without teaching, the prayer remains valid.
The key is the intention (qasd al-ta'leem). The act itself (speaking) is indistinguishable from valid recitation without that intention.
2
Analyze the second ruling: praying Zuhr with worldly motive (dinar)
The Shafi'i case: a person is promised a dinar to pray Zuhr, and he prays with that intention. The ruling according to Hanafi principles: the prayer is valid (because riya does not invalidate fara'id), but he is not entitled to the dinar (because obligatory acts cannot be contracted under ijarah).
This demonstrates the school's ability to extract rulings for novel cases using established qawaid.
3
Examine the underlying qawida: riya and fara'id
The maxim 'al-riya la yadkhul al-fara'id fi haqq suqut al-wajib' means that showing off (riya) does not affect the validity of an obligatory act in terms of fulfilling the obligation. The act remains valid, though reward may be diminished.
This maxim is a dabt (restrictive sub-maxim) applied specifically to obligatory acts.
4
Explore the ijarah dispute on worship
The text notes that early Hanafi scholars considered ijarah for acts like imamah, adhan, and teaching Quran invalid. Later scholars (mutakhkhirin) permitted it due to custom. The mufta bihi is the permissibility, but obligatory acts cannot be the subject of a binding contract that creates an enforceable right to wages.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school, resolved by later authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَقَالُوا: لَوْفَتَحَ الْمُصَلَّى عَلَى غَيْرِ إِمَامِهِ بَطَلَتْ صَلَاتُهُ لِقَصْدِ التَّعْلِيمِ. ترجمه: اور فقہاء فرماتے ہیں اگر نمازی اپنے امام کے علاوہ کولقمہ دے تو اس کی نماز باطل ہو جائے گی تعلیم کے ارادہ کی وجہ سے۔ تشریح: اگر کسی شخص نے اپنے امام کے علاوہ کسی دوسرے کو لقمہ دید یا تو اس کی نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی کیونکہ تعلیم کا قصد پائے جانے کی وجہ سے وہ کلام الناس کے مشابہ ہو گیا اور کلام الناس مفسد صلاۃ ہے۔ ولو فتح على غير امامه تفسد الا اذا عنى به التلاوة دون التعليم (هنديه ج ١ ، ص: ٩٩) وَرَأَيْتُ فَرْعًا فِي بَعْضِ كُتُبِ الشَّافِعِيَّةِ، حَكَاهُ النَّوَوِيُّ فِيْمَنْ قَالَ لَهُ إِنْسَانٌ: صَلِّ الظُّهْرَ وَلَكَ دِيْنَارٌ، فَصَلَّى بِهَذِهِ النِّيَّةِ ، أَنَّهُ تُجْزِتُهُ صَلَاتُهُ، وَلَا يَسْتَحِقُ الدِّيْنَارَ ، إِنْتَهَى، وَلَمْ أَرَ مِثْلَهُ لأصْحَابِنَا، وَيَنْبَغِي عَلى قَوَاعِدِنَا أَنْ يَكُونَ كَذلِكَ ، أمَّا الاجْزَاءُ فَلِمَا قَدَّمْنَا أَنَّ الرِّيَاءَ لَا يَدْخُلُ الْفَرَائِضَ فِي حَقَّ سُقُوْطِ الْوَاجِبِ، وَ أَمَّا عَدَمُ إِسْتِحْقَاقِ الدِّيْنَارِ فَلَانَّ أَدَاءَ الْفَرَائِضِ لَا يَدْخُلُ تَحْتَ عَقْدِ الْإِجَارَةِ، الاتَرى إِلى قَوْلِهِمْ: لَوِ اسْتَاجَرَ الْأَبُ إِبْنَهُ لِلْخِدْمَةِ، لَا أَجْوَلَهُ، ذَكَرَهُ فِي الْبَزَّازِيَّةِ؛ لأنَّ الْخِدْمَةَ عَلَيْهِ وَاجِبَةٌ ، بَلْ أفتى الْمُتَقَدِّمُوْنَ بِأَنَّ الْعِبَادَاتِ لَا تَصِحُ الإجَارَةُ عَلَيْهَا كَالْإِمَامَةِ وَ الْآذَانِ وَ تَعْلِيمِ الْقُرْآنِ وَالْفِقْهِ، وَلَكِنَّ الْمُعْتَمَدَ مَا أَفْتَى بِهِ الْمُتَأَخِّرُوْنَ مِنَ الْجَوَازِ وَقَدَّمْنَاهُ أَنَّهُ إِذَا نَوَى الْإِعْتَاقَ لِرَجُلٍ، كَانَ مُبَاحًا. ترجمہ: اور میں نے شوافع کی بعض کتابوں میں ایک جزئیہ دیکھا جس کو نووی نے نقل کیا ہے اس شخص کے بارے میں جس سے کسی انسان نے کہا ظہر کی نماز پڑھ اور مجھکو ایک دینار ملے گا اس نے اس نیت سے نماز پڑھی تو اس کو نماز کافی ہے اور وہ دینار کا محق نہیں ہوگا، نووی کا کلام پورا ہوا۔ اور اس جیسی بات میں نے اپنے اصحاب کے یہاں نہیں دیکھی اور ہمارے قواعد کے مطابق ایسا ہی مناسب ہے، بہر حال درست ہوجانا اس کی وجہ وہی ہے جو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں کہ سقوط واجب کے حق میں ریاء فرائض میں داخل نہیں ہوتی اور بہر حال دینار کا مستحق نہ ہونا تو اس لئے ہے کہ فرائض کی ادائیگی عقد اجارہ کے تحت نہیں آتی کیا آپ ے تہار کا قول نہیں دیکھا کہ اگر باپ نے اپنے بیٹے کو خدمت کے لئے کرایہ پرلیا تو اس کے لئے اجرت نہیں اس کو
And they said: If a praying person prompts someone other than his imam, his prayer is invalidated due to the intention of teaching. Translation: And the jurists say that if a worshiper gives a prompting (luqmah) to someone other than his imam, his prayer becomes invalid because of the intention of teaching. Explanation: If a person gives a prompting to someone other than his imam, his prayer becomes void because the intention to teach makes it resemble ordinary speech, which invalidates prayer. And if he prompts someone other than his imam, it invalidates unless he intends the recitation (tilaawah) and not teaching (ta'leem). (Hindiyya vol. 1, p. 99)
And I saw a secondary case in some books of the Shafi'i school, narrated by Nawawi, concerning a person who was told by another: 'Pray Zuhr and you will get a dinar.' He prayed with this intention. The ruling is that his prayer is valid, but he does not deserve the dinar. End quote. I have not seen the like among our (Hanafi) scholars, but according to our principles, it should be so. As for validity, because we have established that riya (showing off) does not enter into obligatory acts regarding the dropping of the obligation. And as for not deserving the dinar, because performing obligatory acts does not fall under a contract of hire (ijarah). Do you not see their statement: If a father hires his son for service, he is not entitled to wages, as mentioned in al-Bazzaziyyah, because service is obligatory upon him. Rather, the early scholars issued fatwa that ijarah for acts of worship is not valid, such as imamah, adhan, teaching Quran and fiqh. But the relied-upon position is the fatwa of the later scholars permitting it, and we have mentioned that if he intends emancipation for a man, it is permissible. Translation: And I saw a secondary case in some books of the Shafi'i school, narrated by Nawawi, concerning a person who was told by another: 'Pray Zuhr and you will have a dinar.' He prayed with this intention. The prayer is sufficient for him, and he is not entitled to the dinar. Nawawi's speech ends. And I have not seen the like among our companions, and according to our principles, it is appropriate. Anyway, its validity is due to what we have already explained, that riya does not enter into obligatory acts regarding the dropping of the obligation, and the non-entitlement to the dinar is because the performance of obligatory acts does not fall under a contract of hire. Do you not see their statement: If a father hires his son for service, he has no wages for him.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage presents two interrelated rasm rulings. First, if a person prompts (luqmah) someone other than his imam with the intention of teaching, his prayer is invalid. This is because the act of teaching constitutes speech intended for human communication, which resembles ordinary speech (kalam an-nas) and thus breaks the prayer. An exception is if he merely intends to recite the verse correctly without the purpose of teaching. Second, the passage discusses a Shafi'i casus about praying Zuhr with the intention of receiving a dinar. The author affirms that according to Hanafi principles, the prayer is valid because riya (showing off) does not nullify obligatory acts in terms of fulfilling the obligation; the act remains valid even if performed with a worldly motive. However, the person does not deserve the dinar because obligatory acts cannot be subject to a contract of hire (ijarah). The author then notes the early Hanafi position that ijarah on worship (like leading prayer, adhan, teaching) is invalid, but later scholars issued fatwa of permissibility. The text thus demonstrates how Hanafi qawaid (like 'riya does not affect obligation' and 'faraid cannot be contracted under ijarah') resolve novel cases.

Key Terms
لقمہ (luqmah): Prompting someone in prayer with the correct recitation; if done with teaching intention, it invalidates the prayer.
ریاء (riya): Showing off or performing an act for worldly recognition; it does not invalidate obligatory acts but reduces reward.
اجارہ (ijarah): Contract of hire or wages; obligatory acts cannot be subject to a binding contract for compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because he intended the prayer sincerely
B) Because riya does not affect obligatory acts regarding the dropping of the obligation
C) Because the dinar is a valid compensation for the prayer
D) Because the imam allowed it

Key Takeaway
Teaching intention in prayer invalidates; worldly motive does not invalidate obligation; ijarah on worship is now permitted by later Hanafi fatwa but does not create wage entitlement for obligatory acts.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
The Ruling on Ijarah for Acts of Worship: From Prohibition to Permissibility
Discusses hiring for worship and the intra-Hanafi shift in fatwa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on ijarah for acts of worship and explain why later scholars permitted it, relying on the principle of necessity.

Core Idea
Hiring for worship was forbidden by early Hanafis but later permitted to preserve religious practice.

This passage from a Hanafi usul al-iftaa text presents a classic example of fatwa evolution within the school: the permissibility of hiring someone to perform acts of worship like teaching Quran or leading prayer. The early scholars (mutaqaddimeen) considered such ijarah invalid, but later scholars (muta'akhkhireen) allowed it due to changing circumstances. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its evidence, and the practical difference it makes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is ijarah 'ala al-ta'at? The passage mentions examples: imamah, adhan, teaching Quran and fiqh. State the early Hanafi position and the later Hanafi position.
2
Examine the early Hanafi evidence
The text quotes al-Asl: 'It is not permissible to hire for acts of worship.' Understand the reasoning: wages are for non-obligatory work, and these acts are obligations (wajib) on the doer, so they cannot be compensated.
Analogy to a father hiring his son: son gets no wage because service to father is wajib.
3
Examine the later Hanafi evidence
The later scholars (from Balkh) allowed ijarah on teaching Quran due to neglect in religious affairs. The Hindiyya states: 'they deemed it permissible today because of prevalent negligence; forbidding would lead to loss of Quran memorization.'
The principle: necessity (zuhur al-tawani) justifies a departure from the original ruling.
4
Analyze the related Shafi'i example
A Shafi'i case: person told to pray Zuhr for a dinar. The prayer is valid (because riya does not affect obligation) but the wage is not owed (because it is ijarah on a wajib act). This confirms the Hanafi principle that wajib acts cannot be hired for compensation.
This is consistent with the Hanafi position: the act is valid without wage; for non-obligatory acts, later Hanafis allow ijarah.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text explicitly states that the relied-upon fatwa is that of the muta'akhkhireen: ijarah on acts of worship is permissible. This is the operative ruling for fatwa today.

Source Text

بزاز یہ میں ذکر کیا ہے اس لیئے اس پر خدمت واجب ہے بلکہ متقدمین نے فتویٰ دیا ہے کہ عبادات پر اجارہ درست نہیں ہے جیسے امامت ، اذ ان تعلیم قرآن اور فقہ لیکن قول معتمد وہ ہے جس پر متاخرین نے فتوی دیا ہے یعنی جواز اور کا ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں کہ جب اس نے کسی آدمی کے لئے آزاد کرنے کی نیت کر لی تو وہ مباح ہے۔ تشریح شوافع کی بعض کتب میں یہ جزئیہ ذکر کیا گیا ہے کہ ایک شخص نے کسی دوسرے سے کہا تو ظہر کی نماز پڑھ تجھکو ایک دینار ملے گا اس نے اس نیت سے نماز پڑھی تو اس کی نماز درست ہو جائے گی البتہ وہ دینارکا مشتق ہوگا ، صاحب کتاب کہتے ہیں کہ اس طرح کا جزئیہ اگر چہ ہمارے اصحاب کی کتابوں میں مجھے نہیں ملالہ تہ قواعدکی روشنی میں ہمارے یہاں بھی یہی حکم معلوم ہوتا ہے۔ نماز کا درست ہونا تو اس لئے ہے کہ واجب کے سقوط میں ریاء کو فرائض میں دخل نہیں اور دینار کا مستحق اس لئے نہیں ہوگا کہ یہ اجارہ علی الطاعات کی قبیل سے ہے اور اجارہ علی الطاعات محقد مین کے نزدیک جائز ہی نہیں، جیسے اگر کوئی باپ اپنے بیٹے کو خدمت کے لئے کرائے پر لے تو بیٹے کے لئے کوئی اجرت نہیں ہوگی اس لئے کہ باپ کی خدمت بیٹے پر واجب ہے یہ مسئلہ بزاز یہ میں بھی مذکور ہے اس لئے کہ اجرت غیر واجب عمل پر ملتی ہے اور باپ کی خدمت بیٹے پر واجب ہی ہے۔ عبادات پر اجرت لینے کا مسئلہ عبادات پر اجرت لینے کا مسئلہ در اصل اس بات پر منی ہے کہ طاعات پر اجارہ درست ہے یا نہیں اس کے بارے میں حقد مین احناف کی رائے تو یہ ہے کہ عبادات جیسے امامت، اذ ان تعلیم قرآن اور فقہ و غیر و یا اجارہ درست نہیں ہے۔ وفي الاصل لايجوز الاستئجار على الطاعات كتعليم القرآن والفقه والاذان والتذكير والتدريس والحج والعمرة ولا يجب الاجر كذا في الخلاصة. لیکن بعد کے متاخرین احناف نے ضرور دین کی حفاظت کے پیش نظر امامت ، اذ ان تعلیم قرآن اور فضا غیرہ پر اجارہ کو درست قرار دیا ہے۔ ص:۵۵) و مشائخ بلخ جوزوا الاستجارة على تعليم القرآن (هندیه ج ۴، ص: ۵۵) قال في الهندية و بعض مشائخنا رحمهم الله تعلى استحسنوا الاستئجارة على تعليم القرآن اليوم لظهور التواني في الامور الدينية ففي الامتناع تضييع حفظ القرآن وعليه الفتوى. (شایج میں ) وقدمنا انه اذا نوى الاعتاق : اگر کسی نے غلام آزاد کیا اور غلام آزاد کرتے وقت کسی آدمی کے لئے آزاد کرنے کی نیت تھی تو ایسا کرنا مباح ہوگا، علامہ حموی فرماتے ہیں کہ بات عبادت میں اخلاص کی چل رہی تھی اور اعتباق عبادت نہیں، لہذا ظاہر اس مسئلہ کو یہاں ذکر کرنے کی کوئی وجہ معلوم نہیں ہوتی ، بہر حال اگر اعتاق میں اخلاص نہ ہو تو اعتماق باطل نہیں ہو گا۔
It is mentioned in Bazzaziyya, therefore service is obligatory upon him. Rather, the early jurists gave fatwa that ijarah on acts of worship is not valid, like imamah, adhan, teaching Quran and fiqh. But the relied-upon saying is that upon which the later jurists gave fatwa, i.e., permissibility... And we have already mentioned that when he intended freeing (a slave) for the sake of someone, it is permissible. Explanation: In some Shafi'i books it is mentioned that a person said to another: 'Pray Zuhr for me, you will get one dinar.' He prayed with that intention, so his prayer will be valid, but he will be entitled to the dinar? The author of the book says: Even though such a case is not found in the books of our companions, yet based on the principles, the same ruling appears to apply here. The validity of the prayer is because hypocrisy does not affect obligations, and he will not be entitled to the dinar because this is a type of ijarah on acts of worship, and ijarah on acts of worship is not valid according to the early jurists. For example, if a father hires his son for service, the son will have no wage because serving the father is obligatory. This case is also mentioned in Bazzaziyya, because wages are given for non-obligatory work, and serving the father is obligatory. The issue of taking wages for acts of worship: This issue actually depends on whether ijarah on acts of worship is valid or not. The opinion of the early Hanafis is that ijarah on acts of worship like imamah, adhan, teaching Quran and fiqh, etc., is not valid. (Arabic text: In al-Asl: 'It is not permissible to hire for acts of worship like teaching Quran, fiqh, adhan, reminding, teaching, hajj and umrah, and the wage is not obligatory' as in al-Khulasah). But the later Hanafis, due to the preservation of the religion, deemed ijarah on imamah, adhan, teaching Quran, etc., permissible. (Page 55: 'And the scholars of Balkh permitted ijarah on teaching Quran' - Hindiyya vol. 4, p. 55. Al-Hindiyya says: 'And some of our scholars, may Allah have mercy on them, deemed ijarah on teaching Quran permissible today due to the apparent negligence in religious matters, because forbidding it would lead to loss of Quran memorization, and on this is the fatwa.') And we already mentioned that when he intended freeing: If a person frees a slave and at the time of freeing he intended (freeing) for someone's sake, then doing so is permissible. Allama Hamawi says: The discussion was about sincerity in worship, and freeing (a slave) is not worship; therefore apparently there is no reason to mention this issue here. Nevertheless, if there is no sincerity in freeing, the freeing will not be invalid.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul al-iftaa text discusses the ruling on ijarah (hiring) for acts of worship, a classic point of contention within the school. The author begins by referencing the Bazzaziyya (a fatwa collection) on the obligation of service, but quickly moves to the core issue: the permissibility of taking wages for ritual acts like leading prayer, giving adhan, teaching Quran, and teaching fiqh. He presents the view of the mutaqaddimeen (early Hanafi scholars) that such ijarah is not valid, citing a principle from al-Asl and al-Khulasah. Then he contrasts it with the view of the muta'akhkhireen (later scholars) who, out of necessity to preserve religious practice, declared it permissible. This change of fatwa is a classic example of the Hanafi principle that fatwa can shift based on changing circumstances (taghayyur al-zaman wa al-ahwal). The teacher notes the authoritative weight: early Zahir al-Riwayah positions are superseded by later fatwa due to 'zuhur al-tawani' (prevalent negligence). The passage also includes a related case from Shafi'i sources: a person is told to pray Zuhr for a dinar; the prayer is valid but the wage is not owed, because it is ijarah on an obligatory act (which is not valid). The author analogizes to a father hiring his son for service: the son gets no wage because the service is already wajib on him. This reinforces the principle that wages are for non-obligatory work. Finally, the text touches on intention (niyyah) in freeing a slave: if one intends to free for someone's sake, it is permissible, and lack of sincerity does not invalidate the act (since freeing is not a pure worship). Allama Hamawi questions why this is mentioned here, but the author leaves it as a side note.

Key Terms
اجارہ علی الطاعات (ijarah 'ala al-ta'at): Hiring for acts of worship (e.g., teaching Quran, leading prayer, adhan).
متقدمین (mutaqaddimeen): Early Hanafi jurists (e.g., Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad; up to around 4th/5th century AH).
متاخرین (muta'akhkhireen): Later Hanafi jurists (post-5th century AH) whose fatwa often reflects practical needs.
ضرور دین کی حفاظت (darur din ki hifazat): Necessity to preserve religion – the grounds on which later scholars permitted ijarah.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference – a Hanafi method to depart from an established ruling for a stronger reason.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relied-upon fatwa (mufta bihi) regarding hiring someone to teach Quran?
A) It is absolutely forbidden.
B) It is permissible due to necessity to preserve Quran memorization.
C) It is permissible only if the teacher is a relative.
D) It is makruh.

Key Takeaway
Hiring for acts of worship was initially invalid in the Hanafi school, but later scholars permitted it to ensure the continuity of religious practice.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
10 min
Combining Two Fard Intentions in Worship
Explains the rasm al-mufti rule for combining two obligatory intentions with examples from fasting, charity, and prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rasm al-mufti rule for combining two obligatory intentions to determine which obligation prevails or when the act becomes nafl.

Core Idea
When two fard intentions conflict, the stronger prevails; if equal, choice before starting, else nafl.

This lesson unpacks a critical rasm al-mufti principle from al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair: the rule of combining two obligatory acts in one intention. Understanding this rule is essential for issuing correct fatwas when a worshipper's intention is ambiguous. The source text systematically walks through scenarios in fasting, charity, and prayer, explaining how strength of cause (sabab) determines precedence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two fard acts and their causes
Determine the type and cause of each obligation. A stronger cause (e.g., directly from Allah) takes precedence.
Fard prayers, qada, zakat are stronger than kaffarah, funeral prayer.
2
Check if one is stronger
If one obligation has a stronger cause, the act counts for that obligation.
e.g., qada > kaffarah, fard prayer > janazah, zakat > kaffarah yamin.
3
If equal, apply the choice rule
If both are equal in strength, the person has a choice before commencing the act. If no choice is made, the act becomes nafl.
e.g., kaffarah zihar and kaffarah yamin in fasting or charity.
4
Apply prayer-specific rules
For two fard prayers, the one in time prevails; for two missed, the earlier; for missed and current, the missed unless end of time.
This is from al-Siraj al-Wahhaj.
5
Note the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad holds that combining qada and kaffarah results in nafl, but the relied-upon fatwa is from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (qada prevails).
This is an exception to Imam Muhammad's usual principle.

اقومی ہے اور اگر دونوں قوت میں برابر ہوں پس اگر ہو روزہ میں تو اس کو اختیار ہے۔ جیسے کفارہ ظہار اور کفارہ یمین اور ایسے ہی زکوۃ اور کفارہ ظہار اور بہرحال زکوۃ کفارہ یمین کے ساتھ تو زکوۃ اقومی ہے اور بہرحال نماز میں تو بھی اقومی ہی کو مقدم کیا جائے گا اسی وجہ سے ہم نے فرض نماز کو نماز جنازہ پر مقدم کیا اسی وجہ سے السراج الوہاج میں کہا اگر دو فرضوں کی نیت کی تو وہ اس کے لئے ہوگی جس کا وقت داخل ہو چکا اور اگر دو فوت شدہ کی نیت کی تو وہ ان میں سے پہلی کے لئے ہوگی اور اگر ایک فائتہ ایک وقتیہ کی نیت کی تو وہ قائہ کے لئے ہے مگر یہ کہ وہ وقت کے آخر میں ہو۔
Commentary: In specific acts of worship, combining acts of worship can occur in three forms: (1) combining two obligatory acts in one intention, (2) combining two supererogatory acts in one intention, (3) combining one obligatory and one supererogatory act in one intention. We begin explaining the first type. This combination is either in prayer or in other than prayer. If someone combines two obligatory prayers in one intention, neither prayer is valid; both are invalid because both obligatory prayers, e.g., Zuhr and Asr, are of the same rank and cannot be subsumed into one another, so the intention becomes void. Know that intending two obligations simultaneously, if in prayer, it is void according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and it is a narration from Hasan from Imam (Abu Hanifa). (Al-Bahr al-Raiq, vol. 1, p. 280). And if one intends both qada and kaffarah in fasting, then that fast counts as qada, not kaffarah. Al-Hamawi gives the reason: the stronger cause prevails; qada's cause is stronger because it is from Allah. If one intends qada of Ramadan and kaffarah, it is for Ramadan (Bazzaziyya in margin of Hindiyya, vol. 4, p. 37). According to Imam Muhammad, it becomes nafl, neither qada nor kaffarah. According to Imam Muhammad's principle, the fast should become void because invalidating the description entails invalidating the essence, but here some particulars deviate from his principle. If one intends kaffarah of zihar and kaffarah of oath, since they are of the same rank, he has choice; he may intend whichever he wishes as long as he hasn't started the action. Al-Hamawi says this choice is before commencing any part; otherwise it becomes nafl. Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf also hold this, but Imam Muhammad says it becomes nafl. Al-Hamawi notes that Imam Muhammad's statement is apparently inconsistent because according to him invalidation of description invalidates the essence. If one gives charity intending both kaffarah of oath and kaffarah of zihar, it is taken from whichever he wishes. (Bazzaziyya in margin of Hindiyya, vol. 4, p. 37). And if one intends both zakat and kaffarah of zihar, the charity becomes nafl because the descriptions of both obligations conflict and they are equal in strength, so neither is given preference; neither obligation is fulfilled. In such case, the person becomes a starter of nafl, and he has choice before giving; he may intend whichever he wishes. Or, if the poor person has taken possession but not disposed of it, he still has choice by istihsan. But if the poor person has disposed of it, then he no longer has the choice to specify the intention. (Al-Bahr al-Raiq, vol. 1, p. 280). If one intends both zakat and kaffarah of oath simultaneously, the charity counts as zakat because when two obligations are combined, the stronger is preferred, and zakat is stronger between them. If one intends both a fard prayer and funeral prayer, the fard prayer is valid, because when two obligations are combined, the stronger is preferred. (Al-Bahr al-Raiq, vol. 1, p. 281). And it becomes clear from this that when one intends two obligations, if one is stronger, it is directed towards it. So fasting qada is stronger than fasting kaffarah. If they are equal in strength, then if it is in fasting, he has choice, like kaffarah of zihar and kaffarah of oath. Similarly, zakat and kaffarah of zihar are equal. As for zakat with kaffarah of oath, zakat is stronger. As for prayer, the stronger is also given precedence, thus we gave precedence to fard prayer over funeral prayer. Therefore, al-Siraj al-Wahhaj says: If one intends two fard prayers, it is for the one whose time has entered; if one intends two missed prayers, it is for the earlier one; if one intends a missed prayer and a timely prayer, it is for the missed one unless it is at the end of the time.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explication of a key rasm al-mufti rule: how to handle a situation where a person intends two obligatory acts simultaneously in worship. The author, commenting on the maxim, breaks down the scenarios step by step. The core principle is that when two fard acts conflict in intention, the stronger one prevails. Strength is determined by the cause (sabab) of obligation: an obligation directly from Allah (like qada of Ramadan) is stronger than one that is expiatory (kaffarah). In prayer, a fard prayer is stronger than janazah prayer. If the two are equal in strength (e.g., two kaffarahs of the same degree), the person has a choice before commencement; but if no choice is exercised, the act becomes nafl. For sadaqah, if the intentions are equal (zakat and kaffarah zihar), the act is nafl; if one is stronger (zakat vs kaffarah yamin), the stronger prevails. The passage also notes a disagreement with Imam Muhammad, who in some cases holds that the act becomes nafl or void due to his principle that invalidation of the description invalidates the essence. This is an important exception for a mufti to know when issuing fatwas. The concluding part from al-Siraj al-Wahhaj provides additional rules for prayers: two fard prayers go to the one in time; two missed prayers go to the earlier; a missed and current prayer go to the missed unless it is the end of the time (then current fard takes precedence). The commentary emphasizes that these rules are based on the strength of the obligation and the actual time status.

Key Terms
نية الفرضين (niyyat al-fardayn): Intending two obligatory acts simultaneously in one intention
أقوى (aqwā): Stronger in terms of cause and priority; used to determine which obligation prevails when intentions are combined
اختيار (ikhtiyār): Choice given to the person when two obligations are equal in strength, before commencement of the act

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person intends both a fard prayer (Zuhr) and a funeral prayer (Janazah) in one intention, which prayer is considered valid according to the Hanafi rule?
A) Funeral prayer, because it is a community obligation.
B) Fard prayer, because fard prayer is stronger than funeral prayer.
C) Both are valid, and the person receives reward for both.
D) Neither, because the intention is contradictory.

Key Takeaway
When two fard intentions are combined, the stronger obligation prevails; if equal, choice before start else becomes nafl.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Combining Two Hajjs or Two Umrahs in Ihram: Ikhtilaf and Thamara
Dispute on combining two hajjs/umrahs and its practical consequences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on combining two hajjs/umrahs in ihram and apply the thamara to determine the number of dam due for violations.

Core Idea
When two ihrams are combined, the Shakhayn hold both binding; Imam Muhammad holds only one — the thamara appears in the number of penalties.

This passage from Sharah al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair addresses a nuanced issue in hajj fiqh: what happens if someone enters ihram for two hajjs or two umrahs simultaneously or consecutively? While the general ruling is that such combination is haram, if it occurs, there is a key ikhtilaf among the Hanafi founders regarding the number of valid ihrams. This lesson parses the dispute and its practical consequence (thamara) in terms of the penalties (dam) incurred for violations before starting the actions of hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling on combining two ihrams
The passage begins by stating that combining two ihrams for hajj or umrah is an innovation (bid'ah) and haram as a major sin. For a Meccan (actual or legal) it is a violation; for an Afaqi (one from outside Mecca) it is makruh and against Shariah. This sets the moral context before the fiqh discussion.
Note the distinction between Meccan and Afaqi is a separate ruling not central to the ikhtilaf.
2
Distinguish the positions of Imam Muhammad and the Shakhayn
If someone ties two ihrams of the same type (both fard or both nafl), Imam Muhammad holds that only one is binding: if tied simultaneously, any one suffices; if successively, the later one is binding. The Shakhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that both are binding: he must perform one now and make up the other next year, plus an additional hajj and umrah for the refused (rafd) one.
The Shakhayn differ among themselves on the exact moment of rafd (refusal) of the second ihram. This is detailed in the text.
3
Locate the thamara in the case of violations before starting actions
The practical consequence (thamara) of this ikhtilaf appears when a violation (jinayah) occurs before the person begins the actions of hajj. According to Abu Hanifa, because both ihrams are valid, violations incur penalties for both, so two dam are due. According to Abu Yusuf, since only one ihram is considered binding at that point (the other is already refused), only one dam is due. The text gives specific examples: intercourse, killing game, and being confined.
The thamara is not about the number of binding hajjs but about the penalties.
4
Apply the thamara to specific scenarios
Work through the scenarios: (1) Intercourse before starting: Abu Hanifa → two dam for intercourse + one for rafd = three dam; Abu Yusuf → one dam for intercourse + one for rafd = two dam. (2) Killing game: Abu Hanifa → two valuations (or two dam); Abu Yusuf → one. (3) Being confined: Abu Hanifa → two dam; Abu Yusuf → one. The same ikhtilaf applies to two umrahs.
The number of dam directly reflects the legal status of the two ihrams.

نزدیک ایک ہی ہدی اسے کافی ہوگی۔ و على هذا الخلاف اگر کسی شخص نے ایک ساتھ یا پے در پے دو عمروں کا احرام باندھ لیا تو تعدد احرام حج کی شکل میں جو تفصیل گذری ہے بلا کسی فرق کے وہی ساری تفصیل اس صورت میں بھی ہوگی۔
And if one enters ihram for two hajjs: first, it should be known that combining two ihrams for hajj or umrah is an innovation and is haram as one of the major sins, and it is a violation for the Meccan whether actually or legally, and for the Afaqi it is makruh and against the Shariah. But if someone ties the ihram of hajj upon the ihram of hajj and both hajjs are of the same level, i.e., both fard or both nafl, then there is ikhtilaf among the fuqaha. If he tied both together or successively, then according to Imam Muhammad, if together, only one is binding and fulfilling one suffices; if successively, the one he tied is binding. And according to the Shakhayn, both become binding, and he will perform one now and make up the next year, and he is required to do one hajj and one umrah in place of the one he refused. But as to when the refuse occurs, there is ikhtilaf among the Shakhayn. According to Abu Yusuf, refusal occurs immediately after entering ihram without delay. Abu Hanifa has two sayings: (1) when he starts the actions of hajj, (2) when he turns to one of them, then he is considered refuser of the other. Al-Mabsut says the latter is Zahir al-Riwayah. Abu Hanifa said: when he turns to one of them, he becomes a refuser of the other... And in al-Khaniyah: before he engages in the actions of one of them, Abu Yusuf said: as soon as he finishes the two ihrams, he becomes a refuser of one of them (Tatar Khaniyah vol. 2, p. 541). The fruit of the dispute: when he commits a violation before starting, then he owes two dam for violation of two ihrams, and one dam according to Abu Yusuf. And if he had intercourse before starting, he owes two dam for intercourse and a third dam for refusal, because he will refuse one of them and proceed with the other, and he will make up the one he proceeded with and a hajj and umrah in place of the one he refused. And if he kills game, he owes two valuations, or if confined, two dam. And this same dispute applies if he enters ihram for two umrahs together or successively without distinction. End. Translation: The fruit of the dispute appears in this case: when he commits a violation before starting, then he owes two dam for violation of two ihrams, and according to Abu Yusuf one dam. And if he had intercourse before starting, then due to intercourse two dam are owed, and a third dam for refusal because he will refuse one of them and proceed with the other, and he will complete the one he continues, and a hajj and umrah in its place for the one he refused. And if he killed game, he owes two valuations, or if confined, two dam. And this case is also subject to the same dispute when one enters ihram for two umrahs together or successively. There is no difference in detail between the hajj case and the umrah case. The work of Fath al-Qadir is complete. Explanation: The fruit of the dispute between the Shakhayn appears when such a muhrim, after completing the ihram and before proceeding to or starting the actions of hajj, commits a violation. According to Abu Hanifa, two dam are owed for violation of two ihrams, and according to Abu Yusuf, one dam. And if he had intercourse before starting the actions of hajj, then according to Abu Hanifa two dam are wajib for intercourse and a third dam for abandoning hajj, while according to Abu Yusuf one dam for intercourse and another for abandoning hajj are wajib. And he will make up the hajj in which he did this act, and in place of the one he abandoned, he will make up a hajj and umrah. If he killed game before starting actions, according to Imam Sahib two hadi are needed for becoming halal, and according to Abu Yusuf one hadi suffices. And upon this same dispute, if someone enters ihram for two umrahs together or successively, the same detail that passed in the case of multiple hajj ihrams applies without any difference.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on combining two hajjs or two umrahs in one or consecutive ihrams. It begins by stating that combining two ihrams is generally prohibited (bid'ah and haram) but if someone does it, and both are of the same type (both fard or both nafl), then there is ikhtilaf. Imam Muhammad holds that only one is binding. The Shakhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that both are binding, with the obligation to make up one next year and perform a hajj and umrah for the refused one. The passage then details the timing of refusal (rafd) according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. The thamara (practical consequence) of this ikhtilaf is shown in the penalties for violations (dam) committed before starting the actions of hajj. The text provides specific scenarios: janabah (impurity), intercourse, and killing game. The number of dam differs depending on the ruling on the validity of the two ihrams. The passage also extends the same ruling to two umrahs. This is a clear example of how ikhtilaf among the founders leads to different practical outcomes, which is a key topic in Rasm al-Mufti.

Key Terms
رفض (rafd): Refusal or abandonment of one of the two ihrams, making the person liable for a penalty.
دم (dam): A penalty of slaughtering a sheep or goat for violations committed while in ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Shakhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), if someone enters ihram for two hajjs of the same type, how many hajjs are binding?
A) None, the ihram is invalid
B) Only one hajj
C) Both hajjs are binding
D) It depends on the type

Key Takeaway
The ikhtilaf on multiple ihrams shows how thamara (practical consequence) determines the mufta bihi in hajj penalties.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
6 min
Defining Complete Intention (Niyyah Tamah) in Hanafi Fiqh
Defining the standard for a complete niyyah and clarifying interruptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define niyyah tamah according to the Hanafi school, apply the instantaneous recall test, and distinguish acts that break intention from those that do not.

Core Idea
A complete intention enables instant recall; walking to the mosque does not break it, only acts of i'rad do.

This passage from Rasm al-Mufti literature defines the standard for a valid intention in prayer according to Muhammad ibn Salama. It also resolves an apparent contradiction about acts performed between intention and start. Understanding this rule is crucial for muftis to judge the validity of prayers where intention was made early.

Guided Path
1
Identify the test for complete intention
The person is asked at the moment of takbir which prayer they are performing. If they answer instantly without thought, the intention is complete (tamah). If they need to pause and think, it is deficient and the prayer is invalid.
This is a litmus test for the presence of a focused intention.
2
Understand the condition from Fath al-Qadir
The jurists condition the validity of an earlier intention on the absence of any act 'not from the genus of prayer' between the intention and the start. This seems to conflict with the permissibility of walking to the mosque.
Walking to the mosque is physically not part of prayer, yet the prayer is still valid.
3
Resolve the apparent contradiction
The phrase 'not from its genus' does not refer to any physical act, but specifically to acts that indicate i'rad (turning away from prayer), such as talking or eating. Walking to the mosque is considered a necessary preparatory act, counted as part of the prayer's acts (af'al al-salah), and thus does not break the intention.
This resolution saves the prayer from being invalidated by routine preparatory movements.
4
Apply the rule to different scenarios
If a person, after intending, engages in speech or eating, the intention is broken and must be renewed. If they walk or perform other connected preparatory acts, the intention remains valid.
The key is the indication of disinterest, not the physical nature of the act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَعِنْدَ مُحَمَّدِ بْنِ سَلْمَةَ إِنْ كَانَ عِنْدَ الشَّرُوْعِ بِحَيْثُ لَوْ سُئِلَ أَيَّةَ صَلَاةٍ تُصَلَّى فَيُجِيْبُ عَلَى الْبَدَاهَةِ مِنْ غَيْرِ تَفَـكْرٍ فَهِيَ نِيَّةٌ تَامَّةٌ، وَلَوْ إِحْتَاجَ إِلَى التَّاقُلِ لَا تَجُوْزُ . وَفِي فَتْحِ فَقَدْ شَرَطُوْا عَدَمَ مَالَيْسَ مِنْ جِنْسِ الصَّلَاةِ لِصِحَّةِ تِلْكَ النِّيَّةِ مَعْ تَصْرِيْحِهِمْ بِأَنَّهَا صَحِيحَةٌ مَعَ الْعِلْمِ بِأَنَّهُ يَتَخَلَّلُ بَيْنَهَا وَبَيْنَ الشُّرُوْعِ الْمَشْئُ إِلَى مَقَامِ الصَّلَاةِ، وَهُوَ لَيْسَ مِنْ جنْسِهَا، فَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ كَوْنِ الْمُرَادِ بِمَا لَيْسَ مِنْ جِنْسِهَا مَا يَدُلُّ عَلَى الْإِعْرَاضِ. بِخِلَافِ الْقَدِيرِ“ مَالُوِ اشْتَغَلَ بِكَلَامٍ أَوْ أَكْلٍ أَوْ نَقُوْلُ عُدَّ الْمَشْئُ إِلَيْهَا مِنْ أَفْعَالِهَا غَيْرُ قَاطِع لِلنِّيَّةِ.
ترجمہ: اور محمد بن سلمہ سے منقول ہے کہ اگر وہ آدمی نماز شروع کرتے وقت ایسا ہو کہ اگر اس سے معلوم کیا جائے کہ تو کون سی نماز پڑھ رہا ہے وہ فوراً بغیر غور و فکر کے جواب دیدے تو وہ نیت تامہ ہے اور اگر اسے غور وفکر کی ضرورت پیش آئے تو نماز درست نہیں۔ اور فتح القدیر میں ہے کہ اس نیت کے صحیح ہونے کے لئے فقہاء نے ایسی چیز کے نہ ہونے کی شرط لگائی ہے جو نماز کی جنس سے نہ ہو، حالانکہ انہوں نے اس کے بیج ہونے کی تصریح کی ہے اس بات کے جانے کے باوجود کہ اس کے اور شروع کرنے کے درمیان نماز کی جگہ تک چلنا پایا جارہا ہے حالانکہ وہ اس کی جنس سے نہیں ہے تو یہ ضروری ہے کہ جنس نماز سے نہ ہونے سے مراد وہ چیز ہو جو اعراض پر دلالت کرے، برخلاف اس صورت کے کہ وہ کسی بات یا کھانے میں لگ جائے یا ہم کہیں کہ نماز کی طرف چلنا افعال صلوۃ میں شمار کیا گیا بینیت کے لئے قاطع نہیں ہے۔
تشریح : اس جگہ علامہ ابن نجیم المصر کی نیت نام کی پہچان بیان کر رہے ہیں کہ اس کی پہچان یہ ہے کہ اگر ماز شروع کرتے وقت اس سے اچانک پو چھا جائے کہ کوئی نماز پڑھ رہا ہے اگر وہ غور وفکر کئے بغیر جواب دیتا ہے تو ال کی نیت کامل ہوگی اور نماز جائز ہوگی اور اگر اسے سوچنے کی ضرورت پڑتی ہے تو نیت نام نہ ہوگی اور نماز جائز نہ ہوگی لیکن اگر وہ گھبراہٹ کی وجہ سے نہیں بتلا سکا تو یہ اس کے تحت نہیں آتا ہے۔ وفی فتح القدير : اس عبارت سے ایک اعتراض اور اس کا جواب مل گیا ہے اعتراض یہ ہے کہ مسئلہ یہ گذرا ہے کہ اگر کسی نے نماز شروع کرنے سے پہلے نیت کر لی پھر کچھ دیر کے بعد اسی نیت سے نماز پڑھی تو اس نیت سے نماز درست ہو جائے گی بشرطیکہ نیت اور ابتداء صلوۃ کے درمیان کوئی ایسا عمل نہ ہو جو نماز کی جنس سے نہ ہو حالانکہ
And from Muhammad ibn Salama: If at the start he is such that if asked 'Which prayer are you praying?' he answers instantly without thought, it is a complete intention; if he needs hesitation, it is not valid. And in Fath al-Qadir: They have conditioned absence of what is not from the genus of prayer for the validity of that intention, despite their explicit statement that it is valid while knowing that walking to the prayer place intervenes between it and the start, and that is not from its genus. So it is necessary that the meaning of 'not from its genus' is what indicates turning away (i'rad). Unlike if he engaged in speech, or eating. Or we say walking to it is counted among its acts, not a disrupter.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage provides a precise definition of a 'complete intention' (niyyah tamah) according to Muhammad ibn Salama (a Hanafi authority). The test: if at the moment of starting the prayer, the person can instantly answer what prayer he is performing, the intention is complete. If he needs to pause and think, the intention is deficient, and the prayer is invalid. The text also resolves an apparent contradiction from Fath al-Qadir: the jurists require that between the earlier intention and the start, there be no act 'not of the genus of prayer' — yet walking to the mosque is clearly not part of prayer. The resolution is that 'not of the genus' here means acts that indicate turning away from prayer (i'rad), such as talking or eating. Walking to the prayer place is considered part of the acts of prayer (af'al al-salah) and thus does not break the continuity of intention. This is a delicate point of Hanafi fiqh: an act can be 'not of the genus' in a physical sense but still not count as a break if it is connected to the purpose of the prayer. The tashreeh notes that if hesitation is due to panic (not lack of intention), it does not affect validity.

Key Terms
نية تامة (niyyah tamah): A complete intention that is present and allows immediate identification of the act at start
إعراض (i'rad): Turning away from the intention, indicated by acts like talking or eating that sever the link

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the definition of niyyah tamah from Muhammad ibn Salama, which situation indicates a complete intention?
A) The person can describe the prayer after looking at the imam
B) The person can answer 'Maghrib' instantly when asked at takbir
C) The person recites the fatihah correctly
D) The person remembers the intention after the first rak'ah

Key Takeaway
A complete intention is defined by instant recall at the start, and only acts indicating turning away (i'rad) break it, not preparatory acts like walking.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
The Hanafi Qawida on Intention Concurrency: Principle and Applications
Explaining the qawida on intention concurrency and its furuat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi qawida on intention concurrency, apply it to the cases of walking to the mosque and fasting, and identify when a prior intention is broken by an unsuitable act.

Core Idea
Intention must normally be concurrent with the act; only necessity permits prior intention, as in fasting.

This lesson unpacks a key Hanafi qawida regarding the timing of intention (niyyah) in worship. The rule states that the original position is concurrency, but necessity allows exceptions. We will explore the textual evidence from al-Anfa', the furuat that illustrate the rule, and the condition that an intervening unsuitable act breaks the prior intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Qawida and Its Source
Find the exact wording of the qawida in the passage: 'الاصل في النية ان يكون مقارناً الا عند الضرورة'. Note that it comes from al-Anfa' (a Hanafi work). This is a dabt (restrictive sub-maxim) that governs the rule of concurrency in intention.
The qawida is a wusta (intermediate) rank maxim.
2
Distinguish Real vs. Ruling Concurrency
Understand that 'muqāranah' can be haqiqiyyah (real, at the moment of start) or hukmiyyah (ruling, where a prior intention is considered concurrent if no unsuitable act intervenes). The qawida allows for prior intention only when necessity dictates.
Ruling concurrency is a Hanafi device to validate prior intentions for continuous acts like prayer.
3
Apply the Qawida to the Furu' of Walking to Mosque
The text gives an example: a person intends prayer at home, then walks to the mosque. Walking is not an act unsuitable to prayer (it does not indicate disengagement). Therefore, the prior intention remains valid, and the prayer is correct. This illustrates the exception 'when necessary'.
The ruling is based on Muhammad al-Shaybani's view: prior intention is valid if no unsuitable act intervenes.
4
Apply the Qawida to the Furu' of Fasting
Fasting is a continuous act spanning a long period; concurrency at every moment is impossible. Therefore, the necessity allows prior intention before dawn. This is a standard application of the exception.
Compare with the Shafi'i position, which generally requires concurrency for all acts.
5
Identify the Istithna' (Exception): Acts that Break Prior Intention
The qawida includes an istithna': 'except when necessary'. But the text also clarifies that if an act unsuitable to the worship intervenes (e.g., eating, talking, or any act indicating disengagement), the prior intention is broken. Such acts render the intention void and the prayer invalid.
This istithna' is supported by the consensus (ijma) of the companions as reported in al-Khulasa.
