Oath Intention: Oppressor vs. Oppressed
Maxim on intention in oaths under duress

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'The oath is upon the intention of the oppressed swearer' to determine whether a mufti should accept a sworn party's claimed intention.

Core Idea
The oath's interpretation shifts based on who is the oppressor.

When an oath is administered under duress, whose intention governs? This lesson dissects a key Hanafi maxim that protects the oppressed: the swearer's hidden intention is accepted if he was wronged, but ignored if he is the wrongdoer. You'll learn to identify oppression as the decisive factor in oath rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two parties
In any oath situation, determine who is the halif (swearer) and who is the mustahlif (administrator of the oath).
The mustahlif may be a judge, a plaintiff, or an oppressor.
2
Assess oppression
Decide whether the halif is mazloom (oppressed) or zaalim (oppressor). This status determines the rule.
The key factor is duress or coercion in the oath-taking.
3
Apply the maxim
If the halif is oppressed, his intention (even if contrary to apparent meaning) is accepted. If he is the oppressor, the intention of the mustahlif governs, and the halif's concealed intention is rejected.
The judge or mufti must act accordingly, following Imam al-Khassaf's position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَاعِدَةٌ فِيْهَا أَيْضاً أَلْيَمِيْنُ عَلَى نِيَّةِ الْحَالِفِ إِنْ كَانَ مَظْلُوماً وَ عَلَى نِيَّةِ الْمُسْتَحْلِفِ إِنْ كَانَ ظَالِماً كَمَا فِي الْخُلَاصَةِ. ترجمه نیز ایمان کے بارے میں ہی قاعدہ ہے کہ یمین میں حالف کی نیست معتبر ہوتی ہے اگر وہ مظلوم ہو اور مستخلف کی نیت کا اعتبار ہوگا اگر وہ ظالم ہو جیسا کہ خلاصہ میں ہے۔ تشریح : اس مسئلہ کا خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی ظالم نے کسی کو قسم کھلا دی اور اور اس نے عام کی یا اس کے علاوہ کسی ور چیز کی نیت کر لی جو کہ ظاہر کے خلاف ہوا اور قاضی کو اس کا علم بھی ہے تو وہ اس کے خلاف فیصلہ نہیں کرے گا بلکہ امام خصاف کے قول کو لیتے ہوئے اس کی تصدیق کرے گا اور اگر حالف ظالم ہو تو وہ اس کی تصدیق نہیں کرے گا والحاصل انه لو حلفه ظالم فحلف و نوى تخصيص العام أو غير ذلك مما هو خلال ) الظاهر و علم القاضى بحاله لا يقضى عليه بل يصدقه أخذا بقول الخصاف و أما إذا لم يكن مظلوماً فلا يصدقه . (شامی ج۵،ص:۵۸۶)
A rule in it as well: The oath is upon the intention of the swearer if he is oppressed, and upon the intention of the one who administers the oath if he is the oppressor, as in al-Khulasah. Translation: Also a rule regarding oaths: In the oath, the intention of the swearer is considered if he is oppressed, and the intention of the one who administers the oath will be considered if he is the oppressor, as in al-Khulasah. Commentary: The summary of this issue is that if an oppressor made someone swear an oath, and he (the swearer) intended to specify the general or something else contrary to the apparent, and the judge knows his situation, the judge will not rule against him but will believe him, taking the saying of Imam al-Khassaf. And if the swearer is the oppressor, he will not be believed. The conclusion: If an oppressor made him swear an oath, so he swore and intended particularization of the general or something else contrary to the apparent, and the judge knows his state, he will not rule against him but will believe him, taking the saying of al-Khassaf. And if he is not oppressed, he will not be believed. (Shami vol.5 p.586)
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage presents a methodological rule for judges and muftis regarding the acceptance of intention in oaths. The key distinction is whether the swearer (halif) is oppressed or the oppressor. If he was forced to swear by a wrongdoer, his own intention (even if it contradicts the apparent meaning) is considered, and the court should not rule against him. Conversely, if the swearer himself is the oppressor, his intended meaning is not accepted, and the oath is interpreted against him. The ruling follows Imam al-Khassaf's position, which prioritizes the oppressed party's intention to prevent injustice.

Key Terms
حالِف (halif): The person who swears an oath.
مستحلف (mustahlif): The person who administers or demands the oath
ظالم/مظلوم (zaalim / mazloom): The oppressor or the oppressed; determines whose intention is considered in the oath.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Rule against him based on the apparent meaning.
B) Accept his intention and not rule against him, following Imam al-Khassaf.
C) Ask both parties for evidence before deciding.
D) Consider the intention of the oppressor.

Key Takeaway
When an oath is taken under oppression, the Hanafi school protects the oppressed by accepting his concealed intention, overriding the apparent wording.

The Rule of Substitution of Intention (Niyaba fi al-Niyya)
Discussion on whether one person's intention can substitute for another's in various acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify whether substitution of intention (niyaba fi al-niyya) is valid in a given act of worship and state the Hanafi ruling.

Core Idea
Intention is personal and cannot be delegated; only the actual doer's intention counts.

In Hanafi fiqh, intention (niyyah) is an act of the heart that must accompany the doer. But what if someone else performs the act? Can the principal's intention substitute? This passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair examines three cases: tayammum for a sick person, zakat payment through an agent, and hajj on behalf of another. The ruling consistently affirms that intention follows the doer, not the delegator, with a subtle distinction in hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act of worship
The three acts are tayammum, zakat, and hajj. For each, note who performs the physical actions.
2
Determine who performs the physical actions
In tayammum, a helper wipes the sick person. In zakat, an agent hands over property. In hajj, the agent does all rituals.
3
Apply the rule: intention is required from the person performing the act
Only if the principal directly performs the act does his intention count. If an agent does the physical act, his intention is considered.
In tayammum, the sick person's intention is required despite the helper's actions.
4
Note the exception in hajj
In hajj on behalf of another, the agent's intention is required. This is not considered niyaba fi al-niyya because the agent is the actual performer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تكميل فى النيابة في اليةِ. قَالَ فِي تَيْمم " القِنية": مَرِيضٌ يَعْمَهُ غَيْرُهُ، قَالية عَلَى المَرِبْضِ دُونَ الميم انتهى، وَ فِى الزَّكَاةِ قَالُوا : الْمُعْتَبَرُ نِيَةُ الْمُوَكَّلِ، فَلَوْ تَوَاهَا، وَ دَفَعَ الوَكِيْلُ بِلَانِيَةِ اجْزَاتُهُ، كَمَا ذَكَرْنَاهُ فِي الشَّرْحِ. وَفِي الْحَجِّ عَنِ الغَيْرِ الاعْتِبَارِ لية فَالمُعْتَبَرُ نِيتُه. المَامُوْرِ، وَلَيْسَ هُوَ مِنْ بَابِ النّيَابَةِ مِنْهَا ، لأَنَّ الْأَفْعَالَ إِنَّمَا صَدَرَتْ مِنَ الْمَامُورِ. ترجمه : نیت میں نیابت کے بارے میں تکملہ قضیہ کے باب تیم میں ہے کہ کوئی بہار ہے اوراسے کی دوسرے نے تم کرایا تو نیت مریض پر ہے نہ کہ تیم کرانے والے پر انتھی ۔ اور باب مزکورہ میں فقہا فرماتے ہیں کہ مؤکل کی نیت معتبر ہے لہذا اگر اس نے زکوۃ کی نیت کی ہو اور وکیل نے بغیر نیت کے مال دید یا تواس کی کہانی ہو جائے گی شرح یعنی البحر الرائق میں ہے کہ ہم نے ایسا ہی لکھا ہے اور حج بدل میں مامور کی نیت معتبر ہے اور نیت میں نیابت کے باب سے اس کا کوئی تعلق نہیں کیونکہ افعال تو مامور ہی سے صادر ہور ہے ہیں تو اسی کی نیت معتبر ہے۔ تشریح: مصنف کے کلام سے یہ معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ اس عنوان کے تحت ایسے جزئیات ذکر فرما ئیں گے نہیں میں نیت سے نیابت ثابت ہو جائے گی حالانکہ اس عنوان کے تحت ایسی کوئی چیز ذکر نہیں کی گئی اس لئے مناسب ؟ که مصنف تكميل في دم جريان النيابة في النية كا عنوان قائم کرتے کیونکہ اس عنوان کے تحت ایسے 7 ہے ذكر كئے گئے ہیں جن میں یہ بتلایا گیا ہے کہ نیابت فی النبیہ جائز ہے اور کب نہیں۔ قال الشارح انه لم يذكر عقيب هذه الترجمة شيئا تكون النية بطريق النيابة. چونکہ نیت میں نیابت معتبر نہیں ہے اس لئے قنیہ میں ہے کہ اگر دوسرا آدمی مریض کو نیم کرائے تو خود تمیم کرنے والے پر نیت واجب ہوگی تیم کرانے والے پر نہیں۔ و في الزكواة ز : زکوۃ کی ادئیگی میں موکل کی نیت معتبر ہے وکیل کی نہیں بریں بناء اگر کوئی متوکل نے زکوۃ کی نیت کی اور وکیل بدون نیت زکوۃ مال دیتارہاتو زکوۃ ادا ہو جائے گی۔ و في الحج عن الغير : حج بدل کے ارکان چونکہ مامور ہی سے صادر ہوتے ہیں اس لئے حج بدل کی نیت میں ما مور یعنی وکیل کی نیت معتبر ہوگی اور یہ نیابت فی المدینہ کے قبیل سے نہیں ہے۔
Completion regarding substitution in intention. He said in al-Qunyah regarding tayammum: A sick person whom another makes tayammum, the intention is upon the sick person, not upon the one performing tayammum. End. And in zakat they said: The intention of the principal (muwakkil) is considered. So if he intended (zakat) and the agent (wakil) paid without intention, it suffices, as we mentioned in the commentary. And in hajj on behalf of another, the consideration of intention: so the considered intention is that of the commanded one (ma'mur). And this is not from the chapter of substitution in intention, because the actions are only performed by the commanded one. Translation: Completion regarding substitution in intention. In the chapter of tayammum in al-Qunyah: a sick person whom another makes tayammum, the intention is on the sick person, not on the one making tayammum. End. And in the mentioned chapter, the fuqaha say: the intention of the principal is considered; so if he intended (zakat) and the agent gave the property without intention, it is fulfilled, as we wrote in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. And in hajj on behalf of another, the intention of the commanded one (agent) is considered. And this has no connection to the chapter of substitution in intention, because the actions are only performed by the commanded one, so his intention is considered. Explanation: From the author's words it appears that under this heading he mentioned such particulars that substitution in intention would be established. However, under this heading nothing of that sort is mentioned. Therefore it is appropriate that the author should have set up the heading 'Completion regarding the permissibility of substitution in intention', because under that heading these 7 (things) are mentioned that show when substitution in intention is permissible and when not. The commentator said that he did not mention after this translation anything that would make intention through substitution. Since substitution in intention is not valid, in al-Qunyah it is said that if another person makes tayammum for the sick, the intention is obligatory on the one performing tayammum, not on the one who has tayammum performed for him. And in zakat: in paying zakat, the intention of the principal is considered, not the agent's. Based on this, if the principal intended zakat and the agent gave the property without intention of zakat, the zakat is fulfilled. And in hajj on behalf of another: since the actions of hajj are performed by the commanded one (agent), in the intention of hajj on behalf of another, the intention of the commanded one (i.e., the agent) is considered, and this is not from the category of substitution in intention.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This is a textual unit that presents a rasm rule concerning substitution in intention (niyaba fi al-niyya). The author quotes from al-Qunyah regarding tayammum: if a healthy person performs tayammum for a sick person, the intention must be that of the sick person, not the performer. However, the Hanafi position is that intention cannot be delegated; the sick person must form his own intention even if someone else wipes his limbs. Similarly in zakat, the intention of the principal (owner) is required, not the agent's. In hajj on behalf of another, since the agent performs the physical actions, the intention of the agent is considered; this is not a case of substitution in intention because the agent is the direct doer. The commentator notes that the author's heading is misleading; the examples actually show when substitution is not valid, except for hajj which is a different category.

Key Terms
النيابة في النية (al-niyaba fi al-niyya): The concept of one person's intention substituting for another's in a ritual act
المُوَكِّل (al-muwakkil): The principal who appoints an agent (wakil)
المَأْمُور (al-ma'mur): The commanded one; the agent who performs the act

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man hires a person to perform Hajj on his behalf. When the agent performs Hajj, whose intention is considered for the validity?
A) The employer's intention
B) The agent's intention
C) Both must intend
D) Neither, intention is not required

Key Takeaway
Intention follows the doer; even in delegated acts, the principal's intention is required unless the principal is physically performing the actions.

Rule on Dispute over Willingness in Sale
Ruling on dispute over mutual consent in a sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the ruling on disputes over willingness in a sale by identifying whose statement or evidence is accepted under Hanafi fiqh, and articulate the underlying principle of 'original state' (asl).

Core Idea
The original state in contracts is mutual consent; the one claiming it is believed absent evidence, but evidence of coercion prevails.

This lesson examines a key rule from the Hanafi rasm al-mufti literature regarding disputes between buyer and seller over whether the sale was voluntary. The passage from al-Bazzaziyyah provides a clear evidentiary hierarchy: in the absence of proof, the claimant of willingness is believed because consent is the original state; however, if both parties produce evidence, the evidence of the one alleging coercion is given precedence. Understanding this rule equips you to resolve such disputes in fatwa practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute scenario
The buyers and sellers (mutabayi'an) disagree about whether the sale was conducted willingly (taw') or under coercion (ikrah).
Both parties are assumed to have a claim; the dispute is about the underlying nature of consent.
2
Apply the default rule: claim of taw' accepted
When only claims are made without evidence, the word (qawl) is given to the one who claims willingness because mutual consent is the original and presumed state (al-asl) in contracts.
The principle 'al-asl baqa' ma kana' supports this: the contract is presumed valid.
3
Recognize the exception with evidence
If both parties present evidence (bayyinah), the evidence of the one claiming coercion is superior and accepted.
Coercion is contrary to the apparent state (khilaf al-zahir), so it requires stronger proof; the one alleging it must bring evidence.
4
Understand the rationale
The mufti prioritizes the claim of coercion when evidence is given because coercion is an exception to the default rule and thus demands proof, not mere assertion.
This aligns with the maxim 'al-bayyinah 'ala man idda'a wa al-yamin 'ala man ankar' but here both have bayyinah, so the one whose claim contradicts the asl gets precedence.
5
Note the fatwa consensus
The passage confirms that the mufta bihi position is that the evidence of the coercion claimant is preferred, as recorded in al-Bazzaziyyah.
This is a relied-upon rule in Hanafi fatwa; muftis should apply it in similar disputes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ اخْتَلَفَ الْمُتَبَائِعَانِ فِي الطَّوْعِ فَالْقَوْلُ لِمَنْ يَدَّعِيْهِ لأَنَّهُ الأَصْلَ وَ إِنْ بَرْهَنَا فَبَيِّنَةُ مَنْ يُدْعِي الإِكْرَاهُ أوْلى وَ عَلَيْهِ الْفَتَاوى كَمَا فِي الْبَزَّازِّيَّةِ.
ترجمہ: اور اگر بائع ومشتری کا خوشی سے بیچ میں اختلاف ہوا تو جو رضا ء سے بیچ کا دعویدار ہو قول اس کا ہوگا کیونکہ اصل بیچ میں تراضی ہے اگر دونوں نے بیتہ قائم کیا تو جو جبر کا دعویدار ہے تو اس کا بینہ رائج ہو گا قومی اسی پر ہے بزاز یہ میں اسی طرح ہے۔
تشریح : بائع اور مشتری کے مابین رضا اور عدم رضاء پر اختلاف ہوا تو ایسی صورت میں اس کی بات معتبر ہوگی جو رضا مندی کا دعوی کر رہا ہے کیونکہ یہی چیز اصل ہے اور اگر دونوں نے بہینہ قائم کر دیا تو اس شخص کا بینہ مقبول ہوگا جو اگر او اور عدم رضاء کا دعوی کر رہا ہے اس پر فتویٰ ہے کیونکہ بینہ خلاف ظاہر چیز پر پیش کیا جاتا ہے اور یہاں اکراہ خلاف ظاہر ہے اور خلاف اصل ہے۔
And if the two parties to a sale dispute about willingness, then the statement is of the one who claims it because it is the original state; and if they present evidence, then the evidence of the one who claims coercion is more worthy, and the fatwa is upon that, as in al-Bazzaziyyah. Translation: ... Commentary: ...
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage is a rasm rule concerning disputes between buyer and seller about whether the sale was voluntary or coerced. The ruling states that if only claims are made, the one who claims mutual consent (طوع) is believed, because the original state in contracts is mutual consent. If both parties produce evidence (bayyinah), then the evidence of the one claiming coercion (إكراه) is given precedence, because coercion is contrary to the apparent state and thus requires stronger proof. The fatwa is upon this position as recorded in al-Bazzaziyyah.

Key Terms
طوع (taw‘): Mutual willingness and consent in a transaction
إكراه (ikrah): Coercion that invalidates consent
بينة (bayyinah): Evidence, usually two male witnesses or one male and two females

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The evidence of the one claiming mutual consent
B) The evidence of the one claiming coercion
C) Both are rejected and the sale is void
D) The evidence of the seller is always accepted

Key Takeaway
In disputes over mutual consent in a sale, the default is acceptance of the claimant of willingness; when both present evidence, the claimant of coercion prevails.

Buyer's Claim of Carrion: The Rule of Asl al-Tahrim
Rasm rule: buyer's claim of carrion/Magian slaughter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rasm al-mufti rule that when a buyer claims meat is carrion or Magian slaughter, his statement is accepted due to the original prohibition (asl al-tahrim), and explain the shift in burden of proof.

Core Idea
The buyer's claim is accepted because the original state of the animal is prohibition until lawful slaughter is proven.

This passage addresses a common scenario in the marketplace: a buyer purchases meat and later claims it is carrion or from a Magian slaughter, while the seller denies. How should a mufti resolve this? The classical Hanafi masters have a clear rule based on the principle of asl al-tahrim (original prohibition). In this lesson, we will explore the reasoning behind this rule and how it guides fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and claims
The buyer claims the meat is carrion (maytah) or from a Magian slaughter (dhabihah majusi). The seller denies this. Recognize that the buyer is asserting the meat remains prohibited.
2
Identify the governing principle
The Hanafi principle is asl al-tahrim: the original state of any animal whose meat is generally permissible (like sheep) is prohibition until proper Islamic slaughter is confirmed. This is based on the Quranic verse prohibiting carrion.
This principle is a specific application of the general maxim 'al-yaqin la yazulu bi al-shakk' (certainty is not removed by doubt).
3
Apply the principle to the dispute
Since the original state is prohibition, the buyer's claim aligns with the asl. He is not making a new claim; he is affirming the existing prohibition. Therefore, his statement is given weight.
The buyer is considered a 'mudda'i' (claimant) but his claim is supported by the asl, so he does not need to bring proof.
4
Determine the burden of proof
The burden shifts to the seller, who claims the prohibition has been removed (by lawful slaughter). The seller must prove that the animal was slaughtered Islamically. If he cannot, the buyer's claim prevails.
This is an exception to the general rule that the claimant must bring evidence.
5
Recognize this as a rasm al-mufti rule
This ruling is not from a specific text but derived from the principles of the school. It is recorded in later works like al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair as a guideline for muftis in similar disputes.
The author's statement 'I have not seen it now' indicates it is not in the Zahir al-Riwayah but is from the later fatwa literature.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ ادَّعَى الْمُشْتَرِى أَنَّ اللَّحْمَ لَحْمُ مَيْتَةٍ أَوْ ذَبِيحَةُ مَجُوسِى وَ انْكَرَ الْبَائِعُ لَمْ أَرَهُ الآنَ وَمُقْتَضَى قَوْلِهِمْ الْقَوْلُ لِمُدَّعِي البطلان لِكَوْنِهِ مُنْكِراً أَصْلُ الْبَيْعِ أَنْ يُقْبَلَ قَوْلُ الْمُشْتَرِى وَ بِاعْتِبَارِ أَنَّ الشَّاةَ فِي حَالِ حَيَاتِهَا مُحَرَّمَةٌ فَالْمُشْتَرِي مُتَمَسْكَ بِاصْلِ التَّحْرِيمِ إِلَىٰ أَنْ يُتَحَقَّقَ زَوَالُهُ.
ترجمہ: اگر خریدار نے دعوی کیا گوشت مردار یا مجوسی کا ذبیحہ ہے اور بائع نے انکار کیا تو اسکا حکم نہیں دیکھا اور فقہاء کے قول کا مقتضی بطلان کے دعویدار کا قول معتبر ہے کیونکہ وہ اصل بیع کا منکر ہے کا تقاضہ یہ ہے کہ مشتری کا قول مانا جائے اور اس اعتبار سے کہ بکری اپنی زندگی میں حرام مشتری اصل تحریم سے استدلال کر رہا ہے یہاں تک کہ تحریم کا زوال محقق ہو جائے۔
تشریح : ... مشتری نے دعوی کیا کہ خریدا ہوا گوشت مردار کا گوشت ہے یا مجوسی کا ذبیحہ ہے اور بائع اس کا انکار کر رہا ہے تو ایسی صورت میں فقہاء کے قول کے مطابق بطلان کے مدعی کی بات مانی جائے گی اور اس اعتبار سے بھی مشتری کی بات مانی جائے گی کہ بکری زندگی میں شرعی ذبح سے پہلے حرام ہے کیونکہ اصل بکری میں حرمت ہے جب تک کہ ذبح شرعی سے وہ حرمت نہ زائل ہو جائے تو مشتری گویا کہہ رہا ہے کہ یہ میتہ ہے یا ذبیحہ مجوسی ہے یعنی جو اصل حرمت تھی وہ زائل نہیں ہوئی ہے مشتری اصل حرمت سے استدلال کر رہا ہے کہ اس کا قول اصل کے مطابق ہے اس لئے مشتری کا قول قابل قبول ہوگا۔
And if the buyer claims that the meat is carrion or a Magian's slaughter and the seller denies, I have not seen it now, and the logical consequence of their statement 'The statement is for the claimant of invalidity because he is a denier of the original sale' is that the buyer's statement should be accepted, and by consideration that the sheep in its life is prohibited, so the buyer is holding onto the original prohibition until its removal is verified. Translation: ... Commentary: ...
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage is a rasm rule concerning a dispute where the buyer claims the meat is carrion (maytah) or from a Magian's slaughter (dhabihah majusi). The author notes he has not seen an explicit text on this, but the principle from the scholars' statements is that the one claiming invalidity (batalan) is believed because he is denying the original sale. Here, the buyer is claiming the meat is prohibited, and the original state of the animal is prohibition until lawful slaughter is confirmed. Therefore, the buyer's statement is accepted because it aligns with the original state of prohibition.

Key Terms
ميتة (maytah): Carrion; an animal that died without proper Islamic slaughter
ذبيحة مجوسي (dhabihah majusi): An animal slaughtered by a Magian (Zoroastrian)
أصل التحريم (asl al-tahrim): The original ruling of prohibition that applies before lawful slaughter

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the buyer's claim about the meat being carrion accepted over the seller's denial?
A) Because the buyer is always truthful
B) Because the seller is not reliable
C) Because the original state of the animal is prohibition
D) Because the buyer has witnesses

Key Takeaway
In disputes over meat permissibility, the Hanafi rasm al-mufti rule prioritizes the buyer's claim due to the original prohibition (asl al-tahrim), shifting the burden of proof to the seller.
